Interpretation of the Mutual Harm Prohibition in Quran 2:233
Tafsir of Quranic verse on mutual harm

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the two possible interpretations of 'tudārar' in Quran 2:233 and explain how each reading leads to the same legal ruling that mutual harm is prohibited.

Core Idea
The passive 'tudārar' permits two readings, both prohibiting harm to either parent because of the child.

This lesson unpacks the grammatical and legal interpretation of the key verse on mutual harm. The author explains that the passive form allows two readings: either the mother is harmed by the father due to the child, or the father is harmed by the mother. Despite the reversed order, the legal outcome is identical: no parent may harm the other because of the child. The verse's grammatical form (nasb vs. raf') reinforces the force of the prohibition.

Guided Path
1
Recognize the passive form
Identify that 'tudārar' is the passive form of the verb, originally 'tudārar' with a fatha on the first ra'. The passive allows ambivalence in agency.
The ba in 'biwaladihā' indicates causation.
2
First interpretation: harm to mother
Read the verse as 'a mother should not be harmed because of her child' – i.e., the father should not harm the mother by being harsh, demanding extra maintenance, or grieving her by negligence.
Examples: demanding more wages, taking the child away when she wants to breastfeed.
3
Second interpretation: harm to father
Read the verse as 'a father should not be harmed because of his child' – i.e., the mother should not harm the father by refusing to breastfeed without reason or by causing grief.
The verse can be read with reversed order of the two clauses.
4
Same legal effect
Both interpretations lead to the same ruling: mutual harm is prohibited. The difference is only in which parent is the subject of the prohibition in each clause.
The emphasis is on both parents refraining from harming each other.
5
Grammatical nuance of 'lā tudār'
The verse can be read with nasb (prohibition) or raf' (indicative statement meaning prohibition). Both convey the same legal force, strengthening the prohibition.
This is a common feature of Arabic: an indicative can be used in the meaning of a command or prohibition.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
كتاب الطلاق نفقة الأقارب
ثم قوله له : تكون صيغة مجهول ، فأصلها تضارر - بفتح الراء الأولى – ، والباء في قوله يولدها للسببية، فعلى الأولى يكون المعنى لا تضار والدة زوجها بسبب ولدها، بأن تعنف به وتطلب منه زيادة في النفقة أو الأجرة، أو بأن تحزنه بالتقصير في شأن الولد، وأن تقول له بعدما ألف الصبي بها : اطلب له ظئرا ونحو ذلك.
ولا يضار الأب امرأته بسبب ولده ، بأن يأخذ منها الولد وهي تريد إرضاعه بمثل أجرة الأجنبية أو بأنقص منه ، أو يكرهها على إرضاعه مع عجزها، وإمكان إجارة ظئر أخرى.
وعلى التقدير الثاني يكون المعنى مثل ذلك، لكن مع عكس الترتيب، فيكون معنى : لَا تُضَارَ وَالِدَهُ بِوَلَدِهَا . أن لا يضارها زوجها بولدها، ومعنى: لا تُضَارَ وَلِدَةٌ بِوَلَدِهَا وَلَا مَوْلُودٌ لَهُ بِوَلَدِهِ ﴾ أن لا تضاره المرأة بسبب الولد.
. ومنها : إنه يجب على الأب نفقة أمهات أولادهم بالمعروف ؛ أي بقدر الوسع والطاقة، فإن كانت الأم زوجة لها أو في حكمها فهي بحكم الزوجية، وإن كانت أجنبية بانقضاء عدتها فهي واجبة بناء على الأجرة. ويشهد قوله علة في سورة الطلاق عند ذكر عدّة الحوامل: ﴿ وَأُولَتُ الْأَعْمَالِ أجَلُهُنَّ أَن يَضَعْنَ حَمَلَهُنَّ (۱) إلى أن قال : أَسْكُنُوهُنَّ مِنْ حَيْثُ سَكَنتُم مِّن وُجْدِكُمْ وَلَا تضَارُوهُنَّ لِتُضَيقُوا عَلَيْهِنَّ وَإِن كُنَّ أَوْلَتِ حَمْلٍ فَأَنفِقُوا عَلَيْهِنَّ حَتَّى يَضَعْنَ حَمْلَهُنَّ فَإِنْ أَرْضَعْنَ لَكُمْ فَنَاتُوهُنَّ أُجُورَهُنَّ ) ٩. ومنها : إنّ وارثَ الولد غير الأب يجب عليه ما يجب على الأب، يدلّ عليه قوله : وَعَلَى الْوَارِثِ مِثْلُ ذَلِكَ ، واختلف في تفسيره : فقيل : المراد بالوارث هو الصبي نفسه الذي هو وارث أبيه المتوفى، فيكون أجر رضاعته ونفقته من ماله فإن لم يكن له مال فعلى الأم. وقيل : المراد به الباقي من والدي المولود بعد وفاة الآخر.
ويرد على التفسير الأوّل : إنّ وجوب الإنفاق على الأب إنّما هو إذا كان الطفل فقيراً، فوجوبه مـن مالـه مقدّم على وجوبه على غيره أباً كان أو غيره، ولا يجب على الأب إلا إذا فرض أن ض أنه ليس للصبي ،مال، فلا يحسنُ أن يقال : وعلى الصبي نفقته مثل ما كان على الأب بل الأمر بالعكس.
ويرد على التفسير الثاني : أنه إن كان الباقي الأب فقط ، فالحكم قد سبق أنه يجب على المولودِ له رزقهن وكسوتهن بالمعروف، فيكون ذكره هاهنا تكرار، وإن كان الباقي الأم فقط يلزم أن يكون المعنى، وعلى الأم نفقة الأم إذ أرضعته.
فالصحيح أن المراد بالوراث وارث الصبي من الرجال والنساء غير الأبوين ، فيجبر على نفقة كلّ وارث على قدر ميراثه عصبة كان أو غير عصبة، سواء كان الصبي وارثاً منه أو لا ، كما إذا كانت أنثى يرث منها ابن عمها، ولا ترث هي منه.
وقيد أبو حنيفة لله الوراث بذي رحم محرم ، فخرج به ابن العم وغيره، وذلك لقراءة ابن مسعود : وَعَلَى الْوَارِثِ * - - ذي الرحم المحرم - - مِثْلُ ذَلِكَ [ ] قوله : لَا تُضَار ؛ بالنصب وبالرفع قراءتان، فعلى الأول هو صيغة نهي، وعلى الثاني خبر بمعنى النهي، كقوله : لَا تُكَلِّفُ ) ، وقوله جلالة : يُرْضِعْنَ . [٢] قوله : أوجب دفع الضرر ... الخ ؛ أشار به وبما قبله إلى أن الإخبار في هذه الآية إخبار صورة، ونهي معنى، فتفيد وجوب دفع الضرر عن الوالدين، وحرمة مضارة أحدهما الآخر بسبب الولد ، وللتأكيد في النهي عنها أضاف الله سبحانه الولد تارة إليها وتارة إليه، حيث قال في الموضع الأوّل: يولدهَا ، وفي الموضع الثاني : يولده. إشارة إلى أن عطفها بولدها وعطفه لولده زاجر عنهما. [٣]قوله : فإن امتنعت ؛ أي الأم عن إرضاع الولد وهو تفريع على ما مر من أنّ الآية أوجبت الإرضاع على الأم ، وحرمت المضارة من الطرفين.
[٤] قوله : لا يتضرر ؛ أي لا يحصل له ضررٌ من أن يستأجر مرضعة أخرى غير الأم، بأن كان غنياً يقدر على أداء الأجرة.
Book of Divorce: Maintenance of Relatives. Then His saying: it is a passive form, its original is 'tudārar' with a fatha on the first ra', and the ba in His saying 'biwaladihā' indicates causality. According to the first interpretation, the meaning is: a mother should not be harmed because of her child, by being harsh or demanding extra maintenance or wages, or by grieving the father through negligence or saying after the child becomes attached: 'Find a wet nurse for him' etc. And the father should not harm his wife because of his child, by taking the child away when she wants to breastfeed for a wage equal to that of a stranger or less, or by forcing her to breastfeed when she is incapable while another nurse is available. According to the second interpretation, the meaning is similar but with reversed order: the meaning of 'lā tudāra wālidatun biwaladihā' is that the husband should not harm her because of her child, and the meaning of 'lā tudāra wālidatun biwaladihā wa lā mawlūdun lahu biwaladihī' is that the woman should not harm him because of the child. Among the rulings: the father is obligated to provide maintenance for the mothers of his children in a reasonable manner, i.e., according to capacity. If the mother is a wife or in her ruling, it is by virtue of marriage; if she is a stranger after her waiting period expires, it is obligatory based on wage. This is supported by His saying in Surah al-Talaq when mentioning the waiting period of pregnant women: 'And those who are pregnant, their term is until they give birth... until He said: Lodge them where you lodge according to your means, and do not harm them to straiten them. And if they are pregnant, then spend on them until they give birth. Then if they breastfeed for you, give them their wages.' Among the rulings: the heir of the child other than the father must do what is required of the father, as indicated by His saying: 'And upon the heir is the like of that.' There is disagreement over its interpretation. It is said: the heir is the child himself who inherits from his deceased father, so his breastfeeding wages and maintenance are from his wealth; if he has no wealth, then upon the mother. It is said: it means the surviving parent after the death of the other. The first interpretation is refuted: the obligation of maintenance on the father is when the child is poor, so maintenance from his wealth is prioritized over others, father or otherwise, and it is not obligatory on the father unless it is assumed that the child has no wealth; so it is not proper to say: upon the child is his maintenance like what was upon the father; rather the opposite. The second interpretation is refuted: if the surviving parent is the father only, the ruling has already been stated that upon the father is their provision and clothing in a reasonable manner, so mentioning it here is redundant; if the surviving parent is the mother only, it would imply the meaning: upon the mother is the maintenance of the mother when she breastfeeds him. So the correct interpretation is that the heir is the heir of the child from among men and women other than the parents; so each heir is compelled to pay maintenance according to his inheritance share, whether he is an 'asaba or not, whether the child inherits from him or not, as in the case of a female from whom her cousin inherits but she does not inherit from him. Abu Hanifa restricted the heir to a mahram relative, thus excluding the cousin and others, based on the reading of Ibn Mas'ud: 'And upon the heir, the mahram relative, is the like of that.' He said: 'lā tudār' has two readings: with nasb and with raf'; the first is a prohibition form, the second is an indicative in the meaning of prohibition, like His saying 'lā tukallifu' and His saying 'yurḍi'na'. He said: 'He made necessary the removal of harm...' He indicated by this and what preceded that the indicative in this verse is indicative in form but prohibition in meaning, thus necessitating the removal of harm from the parents and the prohibition of one harming the other because of the child. For emphasis in prohibiting it, Allah attached the child sometimes to her and sometimes to him, where He said in the first place 'biwaladihā' and in the second place 'biwaladihī', indicating that her attachment to her child and his attachment to his child is a deterrent for both. He said: 'If she refuses' meaning the mother from breastfeeding the child, and this is a branch on what passed that the verse obligated breastfeeding on the mother and prohibited harm from both sides. He said: 'He is not harmed' meaning no harm occurs to him from hiring another wet nurse besides the mother, if he is wealthy and able to pay the wage.
Source pages p. 567

Commentary
This passage is an expansion (sharh) on the Quranic verse from Surah al-Baqarah (2:233) regarding the prohibition of mutual harm between parents over the child, and the obligations of maintenance and breastfeeding. The author begins by explaining the grammatical form of 'tudārar' as passive, and the two possible interpretations of the verse: either the mother should not be harmed by the father due to the child, or vice versa. Both meanings are valid due to the ambiguity of the passive form. The commentary then moves to the ruling that the father must provide maintenance for the mothers of his children (ummahāt al-awlād) in a reasonable manner. If the mother is still a wife or in her waiting period, the obligation is based on marriage; if her waiting period has ended, it is based on wages for breastfeeding, as supported by the verse from Surah al-Talaq (65:6). This demonstrates that the Hanafi school uses both explicit Quranic texts and analogical reasoning (qiyas) to derive rulings. The passage then discusses the interpretation of the phrase 'wa 'ala al-warithi mithlu dhalik' (and upon the heir is the like of that) from the same verse. Two interpretations are presented and refuted: that the heir is the child himself, and that it refers to the surviving parent. The correct interpretation according to the Hanafi school is that 'al-warith' refers to any heir of the child other than the parents, who must bear maintenance according to their inheritance share. This includes both male and female heirs, whether they are 'asaba or not, and even if the child does not inherit from them (e.g., a female whose cousin inherits from her). Imam Abu Hanifa further restricts this to mahram relatives (dhū rahm mahram), excluding cousins, based on the reading of Ibn Mas'ud. This is an example of how the Hanafi school sometimes relies on qira'ah shadhdhah (non-mutawatir reading) for takhsis (specification) of a general text. The final part of the passage clarifies the grammatical nuance of the verse 'lā tudār'—it can be read with nasb (as a prohibition) or raf' (as an indicative statement meaning prohibition), both conveying the same legal force. The commentary emphasizes that the indicative form here functions as a prohibition, establishing the obligation to avoid mutual harm. The passage thus combines linguistic analysis, tafsir, and fiqh rulings, typical of a sharh work.

Key Terms
تضارر (tudārār): Passive form of the verb with fatha on first ra', indicating mutual harm between parents due to child.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
What is the legal effect of reading the verse with nasb (prohibition) versus raf' (indicative statement)?
A) Nasb makes it obligatory, raf' makes it recommended.
B) Nasb prohibits harm, raf' permits it.
C) Both readings convey prohibition of harm.
D) The reading with raf' is invalid in Quranic recitation.

Key Takeaway
The verse prohibits mutual harm between parents due to the child, regardless of which reading of the passive form is adopted.

Nafaqah — Maintenance
advanced
12 min
Obligation of Child Maintenance and the Meaning of 'Al-Warith'
Explanation of maintenance obligation and interpretation of 'al-warith'

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to explain why the Hanafi school interprets 'al-warith' as the child's heir (excluding parents) and defend Abu Hanifa's restriction to mahram relatives using the proof from Ibn Mas'ud's reading.

Core Idea
The heir of the child must pay maintenance, but only mahram relatives qualify according to Abu Hanifa.

This lesson examines the phrase 'wa 'ala al-warithi mithlu dhalik' from Quran 2:233. The passage refutes two alternative interpretations (the child himself or the surviving parent) and establishes the correct Hanafi view: the heir is any relative who inherits from the child (excluding parents) and must maintain according to share. Abu Hanifa restricts this further to mahram relatives based on the reading of Ibn Mas'ud. The lesson highlights the school's use of a non-mutawatir reading to specify a general text.

Guided Path
1
Identify the phrase
Locate 'wa 'ala al-warithi mithlu dhalik' in the verse and note that it imposes a maintenance obligation on someone called 'al-warith'.
The context is the breastfeeding and maintenance provisions for the child.
2
First rejected interpretation: child himself
Some argued that 'al-warith' refers to the child who inherits from his deceased father. The passage refutes this: the father's obligation is primary when the child is poor; assigning maintenance to the child's own wealth is illogical.
The child cannot owe maintenance to himself.
3
Second rejected interpretation: surviving parent
Others argued it means the surviving parent after the other's death. The passage refutes this: if the father survives, the ruling is already stated; if the mother survives, it would absurdly require her to maintain herself.
The phrase would be redundant or nonsensical.
4
Correct Hanafi interpretation: heir other than parents
The correct view is that 'al-warith' means any heir of the child besides the parents. They must pay maintenance according to their inheritance share, whether they are 'asaba or not.
Even if the child does not inherit from that heir (e.g., a female from whom cousin inherits), the obligation stands.
5
Abu Hanifa's restriction to mahram
Imam Abu Hanifa specifies that only mahram relatives (e.g., siblings, uncles/aunts who are not marriageable) are included, excluding non-mahram heirs like cousins. This is based on the reading of Ibn Mas'ud: 'wa 'ala al-warithi dhi al-rahmi al-mahrami mithlu dhalik'.
This shows the Hanafi willingness to use a shadhdh (non-mass transmitted) reading for takhsis.

Source Text

ثم قوله له : تكون صيغة مجهول ، فأصلها تضارر - بفتح الراء الأولى – ، والباء في قوله يولدها للسببية، فعلى الأولى يكون المعنى لا تضار والدة زوجها بسبب ولدها، بأن تعنف به وتطلب منه زيادة في النفقة أو الأجرة، أو بأن تحزنه بالتقصير في شأن الولد، وأن تقول له بعدما ألف الصبي بها : اطلب له ظئرا ونحو ذلك.
ولا يضار الأب امرأته بسبب ولده ، بأن يأخذ منها الولد وهي تريد إرضاعه بمثل أجرة الأجنبية أو بأنقص منه ، أو يكرهها على إرضاعه مع عجزها، وإمكان إجارة ظئر أخرى.
وعلى التقدير الثاني يكون المعنى مثل ذلك، لكن مع عكس الترتيب، فيكون معنى : لَا تُضَارَ وَالِدَهُ بِوَلَدِهَا . أن لا يضارها زوجها بولدها، ومعنى: لا تُضَارَ وَلِدَةٌ بِوَلَدِهَا وَلَا مَوْلُودٌ لَهُ بِوَلَدِهِ ﴾ أن لا تضاره المرأة بسبب الولد.
. ومنها : إنه يجب على الأب نفقة أمهات أولادهم بالمعروف ؛ أي بقدر الوسع والطاقة، فإن كانت الأم زوجة لها أو في حكمها فهي بحكم الزوجية، وإن كانت أجنبية بانقضاء عدتها فهي واجبة بناء على الأجرة. ويشهد قوله علة في سورة الطلاق عند ذكر عدّة الحوامل: ﴿ وَأُولَتُ الْأَعْمَالِ أجَلُهُنَّ أَن يَضَعْنَ حَمَلَهُنَّ (۱) إلى أن قال : أَسْكُنُوهُنَّ مِنْ حَيْثُ سَكَنتُم مِّن وُجْدِكُمْ وَلَا تضَارُوهُنَّ لِتُضَيقُوا عَلَيْهِنَّ وَإِن كُنَّ أَوْلَتِ حَمْلٍ فَأَنفِقُوا عَلَيْهِنَّ حَتَّى يَضَعْنَ حَمْلَهُنَّ فَإِنْ أَرْضَعْنَ لَكُمْ فَنَاتُوهُنَّ أُجُورَهُنَّ ) ٩. ومنها : إنّ وارثَ الولد غير الأب يجب عليه ما يجب على الأب، يدلّ عليه قوله : وَعَلَى الْوَارِثِ مِثْلُ ذَلِكَ ، واختلف في تفسيره : فقيل : المراد بالوارث هو الصبي نفسه الذي هو وارث أبيه المتوفى، فيكون أجر رضاعته ونفقته من ماله فإن لم يكن له مال فعلى الأم. وقيل : المراد به الباقي من والدي المولود بعد وفاة الآخر.
ويرد على التفسير الأوّل : إنّ وجوب الإنفاق على الأب إنّما هو إذا كان الطفل فقيراً، فوجوبه مـن مالـه مقدّم على وجوبه على غيره أباً كان أو غيره، ولا يجب على الأب إلا إذا فرض أن ض أنه ليس للصبي ،مال، فلا يحسنُ أن يقال : وعلى الصبي نفقته مثل ما كان على الأب بل الأمر بالعكس.
ويرد على التفسير الثاني : أنه إن كان الباقي الأب فقط ، فالحكم قد سبق أنه يجب على المولودِ له رزقهن وكسوتهن بالمعروف، فيكون ذكره هاهنا تكرار، وإن كان الباقي الأم فقط يلزم أن يكون المعنى، وعلى الأم نفقة الأم إذ أرضعته.
فالصحيح أن المراد بالوراث وارث الصبي من الرجال والنساء غير الأبوين ، فيجبر على نفقة كلّ وارث على قدر ميراثه عصبة كان أو غير عصبة، سواء كان الصبي وارثاً منه أو لا ، كما إذا كانت أنثى يرث منها ابن عمها، ولا ترث هي منه.
وقيد أبو حنيفة لله الوراث بذي رحم محرم ، فخرج به ابن العم وغيره، وذلك لقراءة ابن مسعود : وَعَلَى الْوَارِثِ * - - ذي الرحم المحرم - - مِثْلُ ذَلِكَ [ ] قوله : لَا تُضَار ؛ بالنصب وبالرفع قراءتان، فعلى الأول هو صيغة نهي، وعلى الثاني خبر بمعنى النهي، كقوله : لَا تُكَلِّفُ ) ، وقوله جلالة : يُرْضِعْنَ . [٢] قوله : أوجب دفع الضرر ... الخ ؛ أشار به وبما قبله إلى أن الإخبار في هذه الآية إخبار صورة، ونهي معنى، فتفيد وجوب دفع الضرر عن الوالدين، وحرمة مضارة أحدهما الآخر بسبب الولد ، وللتأكيد في النهي عنها أضاف الله سبحانه الولد تارة إليها وتارة إليه، حيث قال في الموضع الأوّل: يولدهَا ، وفي الموضع الثاني : يولده. إشارة إلى أن عطفها بولدها وعطفه لولده زاجر عنهما. [٣]قوله : فإن امتنعت ؛ أي الأم عن إرضاع الولد وهو تفريع على ما مر من أنّ الآية أوجبت الإرضاع على الأم ، وحرمت المضارة من الطرفين.
[٤] قوله : لا يتضرر ؛ أي لا يحصل له ضررٌ من أن يستأجر مرضعة أخرى غير الأم، بأن كان غنياً يقدر على أداء الأجرة.
Book of Divorce: Maintenance of Relatives. Then His saying: it is a passive form, its original is 'tudārar' with a fatha on the first ra', and the ba in His saying 'biwaladihā' indicates causality. According to the first interpretation, the meaning is: a mother should not be harmed because of her child, by being harsh or demanding extra maintenance or wages, or by grieving the father through negligence or saying after the child becomes attached: 'Find a wet nurse for him' etc. And the father should not harm his wife because of his child, by taking the child away when she wants to breastfeed for a wage equal to that of a stranger or less, or by forcing her to breastfeed when she is incapable while another nurse is available. According to the second interpretation, the meaning is similar but with reversed order: the meaning of 'lā tudāra wālidatun biwaladihā' is that the husband should not harm her because of her child, and the meaning of 'lā tudāra wālidatun biwaladihā wa lā mawlūdun lahu biwaladihī' is that the woman should not harm him because of the child. Among the rulings: the father is obligated to provide maintenance for the mothers of his children in a reasonable manner, i.e., according to capacity. If the mother is a wife or in her ruling, it is by virtue of marriage; if she is a stranger after her waiting period expires, it is obligatory based on wage. This is supported by His saying in Surah al-Talaq when mentioning the waiting period of pregnant women: 'And those who are pregnant, their term is until they give birth... until He said: Lodge them where you lodge according to your means, and do not harm them to straiten them. And if they are pregnant, then spend on them until they give birth. Then if they breastfeed for you, give them their wages.' Among the rulings: the heir of the child other than the father must do what is required of the father, as indicated by His saying: 'And upon the heir is the like of that.' There is disagreement over its interpretation. It is said: the heir is the child himself who inherits from his deceased father, so his breastfeeding wages and maintenance are from his wealth; if he has no wealth, then upon the mother. It is said: it means the surviving parent after the death of the other. The first interpretation is refuted: the obligation of maintenance on the father is when the child is poor, so maintenance from his wealth is prioritized over others, father or otherwise, and it is not obligatory on the father unless it is assumed that the child has no wealth; so it is not proper to say: upon the child is his maintenance like what was upon the father; rather the opposite. The second interpretation is refuted: if the surviving parent is the father only, the ruling has already been stated that upon the father is their provision and clothing in a reasonable manner, so mentioning it here is redundant; if the surviving parent is the mother only, it would imply the meaning: upon the mother is the maintenance of the mother when she breastfeeds him. So the correct interpretation is that the heir is the heir of the child from among men and women other than the parents; so each heir is compelled to pay maintenance according to his inheritance share, whether he is an 'asaba or not, whether the child inherits from him or not, as in the case of a female from whom her cousin inherits but she does not inherit from him. Abu Hanifa restricted the heir to a mahram relative, thus excluding the cousin and others, based on the reading of Ibn Mas'ud: 'And upon the heir, the mahram relative, is the like of that.' He said: 'lā tudār' has two readings: with nasb and with raf'; the first is a prohibition form, the second is an indicative in the meaning of prohibition, like His saying 'lā tukallifu' and His saying 'yurḍi'na'. He said: 'He made necessary the removal of harm...' He indicated by this and what preceded that the indicative in this verse is indicative in form but prohibition in meaning, thus necessitating the removal of harm from the parents and the prohibition of one harming the other because of the child. For emphasis in prohibiting it, Allah attached the child sometimes to her and sometimes to him, where He said in the first place 'biwaladihā' and in the second place 'biwaladihī', indicating that her attachment to her child and his attachment to his child is a deterrent for both. He said: 'If she refuses' meaning the mother from breastfeeding the child, and this is a branch on what passed that the verse obligated breastfeeding on the mother and prohibited harm from both sides. He said: 'He is not harmed' meaning no harm occurs to him from hiring another wet nurse besides the mother, if he is wealthy and able to pay the wage.

Commentary
This passage is an expansion (sharh) on the Quranic verse from Surah al-Baqarah (2:233) regarding the prohibition of mutual harm between parents over the child, and the obligations of maintenance and breastfeeding. The author begins by explaining the grammatical form of 'tudārar' as passive, and the two possible interpretations of the verse: either the mother should not be harmed by the father due to the child, or vice versa. Both meanings are valid due to the ambiguity of the passive form. The commentary then moves to the ruling that the father must provide maintenance for the mothers of his children (ummahāt al-awlād) in a reasonable manner. If the mother is still a wife or in her waiting period, the obligation is based on marriage; if her waiting period has ended, it is based on wages for breastfeeding, as supported by the verse from Surah al-Talaq (65:6). This demonstrates that the Hanafi school uses both explicit Quranic texts and analogical reasoning (qiyas) to derive rulings. The passage then discusses the interpretation of the phrase 'wa 'ala al-warithi mithlu dhalik' (and upon the heir is the like of that) from the same verse. Two interpretations are presented and refuted: that the heir is the child himself, and that it refers to the surviving parent. The correct interpretation according to the Hanafi school is that 'al-warith' refers to any heir of the child other than the parents, who must bear maintenance according to their inheritance share. This includes both male and female heirs, whether they are 'asaba or not, and even if the child does not inherit from them (e.g., a female whose cousin inherits from her). Imam Abu Hanifa further restricts this to mahram relatives (dhū rahm mahram), excluding cousins, based on the reading of Ibn Mas'ud. This is an example of how the Hanafi school sometimes relies on qira'ah shadhdhah (non-mutawatir reading) for takhsis (specification) of a general text. The final part of the passage clarifies the grammatical nuance of the verse 'lā tudār'—it can be read with nasb (as a prohibition) or raf' (as an indicative statement meaning prohibition), both conveying the same legal force. The commentary emphasizes that the indicative form here functions as a prohibition, establishing the obligation to avoid mutual harm. The passage thus combines linguistic analysis, tafsir, and fiqh rulings, typical of a sharh work.

Key Terms
الوارث (al-wārith): The heir of the child (other than the parents) who is obligated to pay maintenance according to inheritance share, restricted by Abu Hanifa to mahram relatives.

Nafaqah — Maintenance
intermediate
10 min
Rulings on Nursing and Maintenance from Quran 2:233
Commentary on Quran 2:233 concerning harm and maintenance for nursing parents

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi rulings on the obligation of maintenance for nursing mothers, the prohibition of harm between parents, and the conditions under which a mother is compelled to nurse, as derived from Quran 2:233.

Core Idea
Maternal compassion implies refusal is due to inability; thus a mother is not compelled to nurse if the father can hire another.

In this passage, the commentator expands on Quran 2:233 to derive detailed fiqh rulings regarding nursing and maintenance. The key issues include the obligation of the father to provide for the nursing mother, the prohibition of causing harm to either parent, and the scenario where the mother refuses to breastfeed. Understanding the Hanafi position on these matters requires careful attention to the Qur'anic text and the reasoning (ta'lil) based on maternal compassion and the concept of 'warith' (heir).

Guided Path
1
Identify the Quranic verse and its apparent meaning
The verse prohibits harm to either parent because of the child and commands the father to provide maintenance. Recognize that the verse is in form a declarative but in meaning a prohibition and obligation.
The two readings of 'la tudarra' (with nasb and raf) both convey prohibition.
2
Understand the ruling on mother's refusal to nurse
If the father can hire another wet nurse without harm, the mother is not compelled to nurse. This is because her refusal is presumed due to inability, based on maternal compassion (ishfaq al-umumiyyah).
If she does nurse, she is not entitled to extra wages beyond maintenance, as nursing is an obligation.
3
Analyze the definition of 'al-warith' in the verse
The correct interpretation is that 'the heir' refers to any heir of the child other than parents, who must provide maintenance proportionally to their inheritance share. Abu Hanifa restricts this to mahram relatives, excluding non-mahram like cousins.
This restriction is based on the recitation of Ibn Mas'ud (radiyallahu anhu).
4
Distinguish between categories of women regarding wages for nursing
A wife (in marriage) and woman in revocable iddah receive only maintenance, not extra wages. An irrevocably divorced woman (bainuna kubra) may be hired for nursing because she is not expected to nurse out of goodwill.
This distinction is based on the husband's action making her estranged.

Source Text

لَا تُكَلِّفُ نَفْسُ إِلَّا وُسْعَهَا لَا تُضَارَ وَلِدَةٌ بِوَلَدِهَا وَلَا مَوْلُودٌ لَهُ بِوَلَدِهِ ) أوجبَ دَفَعَ الضرر عن الأمهات والأباء ، فإن امتنعت والأبُ لا يتضرر) فقيراً، فوجوبه مـن مالـه مقدّم على وجوبه على غيره أباً كان أو غيره، ولا يجب على الأب إلا إذا فرض أن ض أنه ليس للصبي ،مال، فلا يحسنُ أن يقال : وعلى الصبي نفقته مثل ما كان على الأب بل الأمر بالعكس. ويرد على التفسير الثاني : أنه إن كان الباقي الأب فقط ، فالحكم قد سبق أنه يجب على المولودِ له رزقهن وكسوتهن بالمعروف، فيكون ذكره هاهنا تكرار، وإن كان الباقي الأم فقط يلزم أن يكون المعنى، وعلى الأم نفقة الأم إذ أرضعته. فالصحيح أن المراد بالوراث وارث الصبي من الرجال والنساء غير الأبوين ، فيجبر على نفقة كلّ وارث على قدر ميراثه عصبة كان أو غير عصبة، سواء كان الصبي وارثاً منه أو لا ، كما إذا كانت أنثى يرث منها ابن عمها، ولا ترث هي منه. وقيد أبو حنيفة لله الوراث بذي رحم محرم ، فخرج به ابن العم وغيره، وذلك لقراءة ابن مسعود : وَعَلَى الْوَارِثِ * - - ذي الرحم المحرم - - مِثْلُ ذَلِكَ [ ] قوله : لَا تُضَار ؛ بالنصب وبالرفع قراءتان، فعلى الأول هو صيغة نهي، وعلى الثاني خبر بمعنى النهي، كقوله : لَا تُكَلِّفُ ) ، وقوله جلالة : يُرْضِعْنَ . [٢] قوله : أوجب دفع الضرر ... الخ ؛ أشار به وبما قبله إلى أن الإخبار في هذه الآية إخبار صورة، ونهي معنى، فتفيد وجوب دفع الضرر عن الوالدين، وحرمة مضارة أحدهما الآخر بسبب الولد ، وللتأكيد في النهي عنها أضاف الله سبحانه الولد تارة إليها وتارة إليه، حيث قال في الموضع الأوّل: يولدهَا ، وفي الموضع الثاني : يولده. إشارة إلى أن عطفها بولدها وعطفه لولده زاجر عنهما. [٣]قوله : فإن امتنعت ؛ أي الأم عن إرضاع الولد وهو تفريع على ما مر من أنّ الآية أوجبت الإرضاع على الأم ، وحرمت المضارة من الطرفين. [٤] قوله : لا يتضرر ؛ أي لا يحصل له ضررٌ من أن يستأجر مرضعة أخرى غير الأم، بأن كان غنياً يقدر على أداء الأجرة. باستئجار المرضعة لا تجبر" الأم ؛ لأنَّ الظاهر أن امتناعها للعجز ؛ لأنَّ إشفاق الأمومية يدلُّ على أنها لا تمتنع إلا للعجز ، فإذا أقدمت عليه، وتطلب الأجرة لا تعطى ؛ لأنه ظهر قدرتها، فالإتيان بالواجب لا يوجب الأجرة على أنَّ الشَّرعَ لم يوجب للمرضعة إلا النفقة، قال الله تعالى: وَعَلَى الْمَوْلُودِ لَهُ رِزْقُهُنَّ وَكِسْوَتُهُنَّ بالمعروف ) ، فكلُّ مَن يأخذ النفقة، وهي المنكوحة ومعتدةُ الرَّجعي لا تعطى شيئاً آخر للإرضاع، وأما المبتوتة فكذا في رواية، وأما على الرّواية الأخرى فإن الزوج قد أوحشها بالإبانة ، فلا ترجى منها المسامحة والمساهلة، فصارت كما بعد العدة، [۱] قوله : لا تجبر؛ أي لا يجبرها القاضي بإرضاع الولد، أو لا يجبرها الوالد به. [٢] قوله : لأن الظاهر ... الخ ؛ حاصله : أنّ المحبّة واللطف الذي يكون للأمهات بأولادهن يقتضي أنها لا تنكر إرضاعهم إلا بعذر وعجز. [٦] (۳) قوله : فإذا أقدمت ؛ من الإقدام بمعنى الإقبال والتوجه ؛ أي إذا لم تمتنع الأم من إرضاعه بل أقبلت عليه، فقد أتت بما وجب عليه ، فلا تستحق الأجرة بالإرضاع ؛ لأن الواجب شرعاً لا يجب بعوضه الأجرة. (٤) قوله : لا يوجب الأجرة ؛ وإنّما تجب الأجرة إذا عقدت الإجارة على فعل هو في سعة من فعله أو تركه. [0] قوله : على أن...الخ ؛ علاوة على ما مر لإثباتِ أنّ الأم لا تعطى الأجرة على الإرضاع، وحاصله : إنّ الشارع لم يوجب على الأب إلا النفقة للتي ترضع الولد، حيث قال : وَعَلَى الْمَوْلُودِ لَهُ * - - أي الأب - - رِزْقُهُنَّ ؛ أي رزق الوالدات المرضعات، ولم يذكر أنّ نفقة الرضاعة غير نفقة الروجيّة ، فلا تجب عليه للمرضعات إلا نفقة لا أزيد منها. [٦]قوله : فإنّ الزوج ...الخ ؛ حاصل هذا التعليل أنّ الزوجَ لَمَّا أبانها وطلَّقَها طلاقاً لا يحتمل الرجوع أوحشها ؛ أي دخلها في وحشة الفراق والانقطاع، ومثل هذه التي توحشت بفعله لا يرجى منها أن تسامح وتساهله فترضع ولده من غير أن تأخذ زيادة على نفقة العدة، فتجوزُ إجارتها لإرضاع ولده، كما تجوز إجارة الأمّ إذا . طلقت وانقضت عدتها وصارت أجنبية.
No soul shall be burdened beyond its capacity. No mother shall be harmed through her child, nor father through his child. (This) obligated the removal of harm from mothers and fathers. If the mother refuses and the father is not harmed (i.e., he is wealthy), then his obligation from his own wealth takes precedence over its obligation on others, be it the father or other. It is not obligatory on the father except if it is assumed that the child has no wealth. So it is not proper to say: The child's maintenance is like what was on the father; rather the opposite. And the second interpretation is refuted: If only the father remains, the ruling has preceded that it is obligatory on the one to whom the child is born (the father) to provide their provision and clothing in a reasonable manner, so his mention here is repetition. If only the mother remains, it would necessitate the meaning: on the mother is the maintenance of the mother when she nurses him. So the correct interpretation is that by 'the heir' is meant the heir of the child from among men and women other than the parents. So every heir is compelled to provide maintenance according to the measure of his inheritance, whether asabah or not, whether the child inherits from him or not, as when a female is such that her cousin inherits from her, but she does not inherit from him. Abu Hanifa restricted 'the heir' to a mahram relative, thus excluding the cousin and others. This is due to the recitation of Ibn Mas'ud: 'And upon the heir - the mahram relative - the like of that.' He said: 'لا تضار' with nasb and with raf' are two recitations. According to the first, it is a prohibitive form; according to the second, it is a declarative sentence meaning prohibition, like His saying 'لا تكلف' and His majestic saying 'يرضعن'. He said: 'Obligated the removal of harm... etc.' - he indicated by this and what preceded that the informing in this verse is in form, but prohibition in meaning, so it conveys the obligation of removing harm from the parents and the prohibition of one harming the other because of the child. And to emphasize the prohibition, Allah added the child sometimes to her and sometimes to him, where He said in the first place: 'her child', and in the second place: 'his child', indicating that linking her to her child and him to his child is a deterrent for both. He said: 'If she refuses' - i.e., the mother from nursing the child, and this is a branch of what preceded that the verse obligated nursing on the mother and prohibited harm from both sides. He said: 'He is not harmed' - i.e., no harm occurs to him from hiring another wet nurse other than the mother, if he is wealthy and able to pay the wage. By hiring the wet nurse, the mother is not compelled, because apparently her refusal is due to inability; because maternal compassion indicates that she does not refuse except due to inability. So if she proceeds (to nurse) and demands wages, she is not given, because her ability is apparent; performing an obligation does not entitle one to wages. Moreover, the law has not obligated for the nurse except maintenance. Allah said: 'And upon the one to whom the child is born is their provision and clothing in a reasonable manner.' So everyone who takes maintenance - i.e., the wife and the woman in revocable iddah - is not given anything extra for nursing. As for the irrevocably divorced woman, it is similar in one narration; but in the other narration, indeed the husband has made her feel estranged by the irrevocable divorce, so leniency and concession are not expected from her; thus she becomes like one after the iddah. He said: 'She is not compelled' - i.e., the judge does not compel her to nurse the child, or the father does not compel her. He said: 'Because apparently... etc.' - its summary: that the love and kindness that mothers have for their children necessitate that they do not refuse to nurse them except due to an excuse and inability. (3) He said: 'When she proceeds' - from 'iqdam' meaning coming forward and turning; i.e., if the mother does not refuse but rather proceeds to nurse, she has performed what was obligatory upon her, so she does not deserve wages for nursing, because what is legally obligatory does not require compensation. (4) He said: 'does not necessitate wages' - wages are only due when a hiring contract is made for an act which one is at liberty to do or leave. (0) He said: 'Moreover... etc.' - in addition to what preceded to prove that the mother is not given wages for nursing. Its summary: the Lawgiver did not obligate on the father except maintenance for the one who nurses the child, as He said 'And upon the one to whom the child is born' (i.e., the father) 'their provision', i.e., the provision of the nursing mothers; and He did not mention that the wage of nursing is different from the maintenance of marriage, so nothing more than maintenance is obligatory on him for the nursing mothers. (6) He said: 'Indeed the husband... etc.' - the summary of this reasoning: When the husband issued an irrevocable divorce and divorced her with a divorce that does not permit return, he made her feel estranged, i.e., she entered into the estrangement of separation and severance. Such a woman, who has become estranged by his action, is not expected to be lenient and accommodating to nurse his child without taking extra beyond the iddah maintenance. So it is permissible to hire her to nurse his child, just as it is permissible to hire the mother if she is divorced and her iddah has expired and she becomes a stranger.
Source pages p. 568

Commentary
This passage is a commentary (sharh) on the Quranic verse 2:233, which deals with the rights and obligations of parents regarding nursing and maintenance of children. The author begins by affirming that the verse prohibits harm to either parent because of the child, and obligates the father to provide maintenance for the nursing mother. The discussion then turns to the interpretation of the word 'الوراث' (the heir) in the verse. The correct view, according to the text, is that 'the heir' refers to any heir of the child (other than the parents) who inherits from the child, and such an heir can be compelled to provide maintenance proportional to their inheritance share. However, Abu Hanifa restricts this to mahram relatives (those with whom marriage is permanently prohibited due to blood relations), thus excluding non-mahram relatives like a cousin. This restriction is based on the recitation of Ibn Mas'ud which adds 'ذي رحم محرم' (the mahram relative). Next, the commentary explains the reading of 'لا تضار' (with nasb or raf') and its implication that the verse is actually a prohibition in meaning. The author then addresses the scenario where the mother refuses to breastfeed. If the father is wealthy and can hire another wet nurse without being harmed (i.e., hardship), the mother is not compelled to nurse. The reason is that maternal love suggests she would only refuse due to genuine inability. If she does proceed to nurse, she is not entitled to extra wages beyond her regular maintenance (nafaqa) because nursing is her obligation. The text distinguishes between different categories of women: the wife (in a valid marriage) and the woman in revocable iddah are not paid extra; the irrevocably divorced woman (bainuna kubra) may be hired for nursing because she is no longer entitled to full maintenance and cannot be expected to nurse out of goodwill. This is the Hanafi ruling on the matter.

Key Terms
الوراث (al-warith): In this passage, 'al-warith' refers to the heir of the child who inherits from him/her. It is interpreted as any heir other than the parents, but Abu Hanifa restricts it to a mahram relative.
ذي رحم محرم (dhi rahm mahram): A mahram relative, i.e., a person with whom marriage is permanently prohibited due to blood relationship (e.g., father, brother, uncle, etc.).
إشفاق الأمومية (ishfaq al-umumiyyah): Maternal compassion or affection that naturally inclines a mother to care for her child, used here as evidence that her refusal to nurse is due to inability, not unwillingness.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the Hanafi position in this passage, if the mother refuses to breastfeed the child and the father is wealthy enough to hire another wet nurse, what is the ruling?
A) The mother is compelled to breastfeed by the judge.
B) The mother is not compelled, and the father must hire another wet nurse.
C) The mother must breastfeed unless she has a medical excuse.
D) The father can deduct the cost of the wet nurse from the mother's maintenance.

Key Takeaway
The Hanafi school holds that a mother is not compelled to nurse if the father can afford a wet nurse, and the obligation of maintenance for nursing is on the father and restricted mahram heirs.

Nafaqah — Maintenance
intermediate
12 min
Wages for a Nursing Mother: When Maintenance Precludes Extra Payment
Explains when mother is entitled to wages for nursing her child.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi ruling on wages for a mother nursing her child and apply the distinction between maintenance and wages based on marital status and iddah.

Core Idea
A mother is not entitled to extra wages for nursing during marriage or revocable iddah because maintenance covers it; after irrevocable divorce, two narrations exist.

This passage from 'Umdat al-Ri'ayah clarifies when a mother can demand wages for nursing her own child. The key is whether she is already receiving maintenance from the father. The Quranic verses provide the foundational distinction: maintenance during marriage and iddah, wages after iddah. The internal Hanafi disagreement on the irrevocably divorced mother highlights the school's nuanced approach.

Guided Path
1
Identify the Act and Its Default Ruling
Recognize that nursing is a religious obligation (wajib) on the mother when able. The default rule is that performing a wajib does not entitle one to wages.
2
Distinguish the Three Scenarios
Differentiate between: (1) wife or revocably divorced mother (maintenance due), (2) irrevocably divorced mother in iddah (two narrations), (3) mother after iddah (estranged, no maintenance).
3
Apply the Quranic Proofs
Use Surah al-Baqarah 2:233 to establish that maintenance covers nursing during marriage/iddah. Use Surah al-Talaq 65:6 to prove that after iddah, wages become obligatory.
The second verse is explicit (nass) about giving wages after iddah.
4
Analyze the Internal Hanafi Ikhtilaf
Examine the two narrations for the irrevocably divorced mother: one denies extra wages (like revocably divorced), another grants them due to estrangement. Understand the reasoning behind each.
The mufta bihi is often the second view, but both are transmitted.

(۱) الطلاق : من الآية .
Book of Divorce: Maintenance of Relatives. (1) [3] 569: By hiring a wet nurse, the mother is not compelled [to nurse]; because the apparent situation is that her refusal is due to inability, since maternal affection indicates that she would not refuse except due to inability. So if she proceeds to nurse and demands wages, she is not given [them] because her ability has become apparent; performing an obligation does not necessitate wages. Moreover, the Lawgiver has not obligated for the wet nurse except maintenance. Allah Most High said: 'Upon the one to whom the child is born is their provision and clothing according to what is reasonable.' So everyone who takes maintenance—the married woman and the woman in a revocable iddah—is not given anything extra for nursing. As for the irrevocably divorced woman, it is similar in one narration. But according to the other narration, the husband has estranged her by the irrevocable divorce, so leniency and ease are not expected from her; thus she becomes like [a woman] after the iddah. [1] His saying: 'is not compelled' means the judge does not compel her to nurse the child, or the father does not compel her to do so. [2] His saying: 'because the apparent...etc.': the gist is that the love and affection that mothers have for their children necessitate that they would not refuse to nurse them except due to an excuse or inability. [6] (3) His saying: 'so if she proceeds' from 'proceeding' meaning coming forward and turning to; i.e., if the mother does not refuse to nurse him but rather proceeds to do so, she has performed what was obligatory upon her, so she does not deserve wages for nursing because a legally obligatory act does not require compensation as wages. (4) His saying: 'does not necessitate wages': wages are only obligatory if a contract of hire is made for an action that one has the option to do or not do. [0] His saying: 'Moreover...etc.': in addition to what has passed to prove that the mother is not given wages for nursing. The gist is that the Lawgiver has not obligated upon the father except maintenance for the one who nurses the child, where He said: 'Upon the one to whom the child is born'—i.e., the father—'their provision'—i.e., the provision of the nursing mothers—and He did not mention that the maintenance of nursing is separate from the maintenance of marriage, so nothing more than maintenance is obligated upon him for the nursing mothers. [6] His saying: 'for the husband...etc.': the gist of this reasoning is that when the husband divorced her irrevocably, a divorce that does not admit of return, he estranged her, i.e., she entered into the estrangement of separation and disconnection. Such a woman, who has been estranged by his action, it is not expected that she will be lenient and easy with him to nurse his child without taking extra beyond the iddah maintenance. So hiring her to nurse his child is permissible, just as hiring the mother is permissible when she has been divorced and her iddah has ended and she has become a stranger. (1) From Surat al-Baqarah, verse 233. [PAGE_570] 570: 'Umdat al-Ri'ayah 'ala Sharh al-Wiqayah. 'And for nursing him after the iddah or for his son from another woman, it is valid.' Hiring is only permissible after the iddah because maintenance is not obligatory for her, so wages become obligatory due to His saying 'and upon the one to whom the child is born is their provision' etc. [2] [3] 'And for nursing him after the iddah or for his son from another woman, it is valid': i.e., hiring her to nurse his child who is from her after he has divorced her and her iddah has expired. The answer to this is: although the husband has estranged her, as long as she is in the iddah she is not completely cut off from him, and her maintenance is obligatory on him, so nothing extra is obligated for nursing if she proceeds to do it, unlike after the iddah. [1] His saying: 'Hiring is only permissible...etc.': a rebuttal of a presumed objection. The presumed objection is that they have explicitly stated the permissibility of hiring after the expiration of the iddah and the obligation of giving wages for it, even though nursing is obligatory upon mothers by the text, so wages should not be obligatory. The gist of the rebuttal: Just as the Lawgiver obligated nursing upon mothers, He also obligated upon fathers the provision and clothing of nursing mothers in the customary manner. Since the maintenance and clothing of the married woman and the woman in iddah are obligatory on him by reason of marriage or iddah, nothing extra is obligated upon him for nursing; thus hiring them for it is not permissible. When the iddah ends and she becomes a stranger to the father, her maintenance and clothing are not obligatory on the father; so if she proceeds to nurse, her maintenance in the customary manner becomes obligatory on him; therefore hiring her for it is permissible. [2] His saying: 'due to His saying', and His saying in Surat al-Talaq: 'Then if they nurse [the child] for you, give them their due payment' (1). This proof is more appropriate than the previous verse, because the verse of Surat al-Talaq is explicit about the permissibility of hiring mothers whose iddah has expired and the obligation of giving them their wages. [3] His saying: 'or for his son' i.e., to nurse his son born from another wife other than this wife. [4] His saying: 'to nurse his child who is from her' i.e., who is born from her womb; from this the ruling of hiring a woman whose iddah has expired to nurse his child from another woman is known by primary inference. (1) Al-Talaq: from the verse.
Source pages p. 569

Commentary
This is a commentary passage from 'Umdat al-Ri'ayah explaining the ruling on wages for a mother nursing her child. The passage begins by stating that a mother cannot be compelled to nurse her child if she refuses, because her refusal is assumed to be due to inability (maternal affection would otherwise compel her). If she then agrees to nurse and demands wages, she is not given them because she is performing an obligatory act, and obligatory acts do not entitle one to wages. The author then provides the Quranic proof (Surah al-Baqarah 2:233) that the father must provide maintenance and clothing to the nursing mothers, but no extra wages for nursing. This applies to the wife and the revocably divorced woman during her iddah, as they already receive maintenance. For the irrevocably divorced woman (ba'in), there are two narrations in the Hanafi school: one that she is also not entitled to extra wages (like the revocably divorced), and another that she is, because the husband's action estranged her and leniency is not expected. The commentary explains that after the iddah ends, the mother is a stranger, so maintenance is no longer obligatory; thus hiring her for wages is valid. A presumed objection is addressed: nursing is obligatory on mothers by Quranic text, so why would wages be given? The rebuttal is that while nursing is obligatory, fathers are also obligated to provide for nursing mothers; for those already receiving maintenance (wife, iddah), no extra is due, but after iddah, since no maintenance is due, wages become obligatory. The verse from Surah al-Talaq (65:6) is cited as explicit proof for this.

Key Terms
مبتوتة (mabtūtah): A woman divorced irrevocably (ba'in), i.e., a divorce that does not allow the husband to take her back without a new marriage.
إجارة (ijārah): A contract of hire for a specific service, here nursing, with a fixed wage.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the passage, when is a mother entitled to wages for nursing her child?
A) During marriage
B) During revocable iddah
C) After her iddah expires following an irrevocable divorce
D) Never

Key Takeaway
A mother's entitlement to wages for nursing depends on whether she already receives maintenance from the father; after complete separation (after iddah), wages are due.

Father's Obligation for Adult Daughter and Disabled Son
Ruling on father's nafaqa for adult daughter and disabled son

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the conditions under which a father is obligated to provide nafaqa for his adult daughter and disabled son, and identify when the obligation ends.

Core Idea
A father owes maintenance to an adult unmarried daughter and a permanently disabled son because they are incapable of earning.

This lesson examines the Hanafi ruling on a father's obligation to support his adult daughter and disabled son. The source text from 'Umdat al-Ri'ayah clarifies that the obligation is independent of the daughter's earning capacity, as femininity itself is considered an inherent incapacity. For the son, only a chronic disability triggers the obligation. We will explore the conditions and scope of this ruling.

Guided Path
1
Identify the act and its ruling
The act is the father providing maintenance (nafaqa). The ruling is wajib (obligatory) upon the father.
The matn states 'especially upon the father' (على الأب خاصة).
2
List the conditions for each dependent
For the daughter: she must be adult (balighah) and unmarried. For the son: he must be disabled (zamin) – someone with a chronic illness or condition that prevents earning.
The commentary defines 'zamin' as blindness, paralysis, etc.
3
Understand the rationale for the daughter
The commentary says 'femininity is absolute incapacity' (الأنوثة مطلقاً عجز). Even if she can earn, the obligation remains.
This is a key Hanafi principle: the daughter's gender alone is sufficient cause for maintenance.
4
Identify the termination of the father's obligation for the daughter
The father's obligation ends when the daughter marries; then the husband becomes responsible.
After marriage, nafaqa shifts to the husband (نفقتها على الزوج دون الأب).
5
Note the fatwa status
The text ends with 'به يفتى' – this is the relied-upon fatwa (mufta bihi).
This indicates the ruling is established and operative in the Hanafi school.

Source Text

And the maintenance of an adult daughter and a disabled son is especially upon the father; this is the fatwa. [٤] His statement: 'adult' is a condition of the daughter, and by it he indicates that femininity is absolute incapacity, so the maintenance of the daughter is obligatory even if she is able to earn, and this is as long as she is not married. After marriage, her maintenance is obligatory upon the husband, not the father. Source pages p. 571

Commentary
This passage contains a ruling on the father's obligation to provide maintenance (nafaqa) for his adult daughter and permanently disabled son. The matn states this is especially on the father, and this is the relied-upon fatwa. The commentary clarifies that the term 'adult' (balighah) describes the daughter, and the reason she is entitled to maintenance even if she can earn is that femininity is considered an inherent incapacity for work. Her maintenance remains on the father until she marries, after which it shifts to the husband. For the son, the condition is that he is 'zamin' (chronically disabled) - defined as someone with a permanent illness preventing earning, like blindness or paralysis. This ruling reflects the Hanafi principle that nafaqa is wajib on the father for dependents who cannot support themselves.

Key Terms
نفقة (nafaqah): Maintenance including food, clothing, and shelter.
بالغة (bāligḥah): A female who has reached puberty and adulthood.
زَمِن (zamin): A person with a chronic disability that prevents earning, such as blindness or paralysis.

Key Takeaway

Nafaqah — Maintenance

Mother's Nursing Priority and Maintenance of Adult Daughter and Disabled Son: Hanafi Positions and Dispute
Rulings on mother's nursing and father's maintenance obligation with internal Hanafi disagreement

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi ruling on mother's priority in nursing and the maintenance of an adult daughter and disabled son, and explain the intra-Hanafi dispute regarding the division of maintenance.

Core Idea
In Hanafi law, the mother has priority to nurse her child at a fair wage, and the father bears the full maintenance of an adult unmarried daughter and a chronically disabled son.

This lesson examines two key rulings on family maintenance (nafaqah) from the Hanafi school. First, we explore the mother's right to nurse her child and the condition that she cannot demand wages higher than a stranger. Second, we look at the obligation to support adult children — an unmarried daughter and a chronically disabled son — where the relied-upon Hanafi view places full responsibility on the father. However, a notable intra-madhhab disagreement exists, which we will analyze to understand how different evidence shapes divergent positions.

Guided Path
1
Identify the two rulings in the matn
Locate the two clear rulings stated in the base text: the mother's entitlement to nurse (with the exception of demanding excessive wages) and the obligation of maintenance for an adult daughter and a disabled son being specifically on the father.
These two rulings are introduced by 'وهي أحق من الأجنبية إلا إذا طلبت زيادة أجرة' and 'ونفقة البنت بالغة والابن زمنا على الأب خاصة'.
2
Trace the evidence for the mother's nursing priority
The commentator derives the mother's right from Quran 2:233, which prohibits harming parents over nursing. The ruling is qualified: she is only entitled if she demands no wage or a wage equal to or less than that of a stranger.
The key condition is highlighted in the commentary: if she demands more, the stranger takes priority.
3
Distinguish the maintenance ruling as the apparent narration
The matn states that maintenance of an adult daughter and disabled son is exclusively on the father, and the commentator confirms this is the position given fatwa (zāhir al-riwāyah). Note the rationale: femaleness is considered a disability, so the daughter's maintenance is wajib even if she can earn; for the disabled son, inability to earn triggers the father's obligation.
The daughter's maintenance shifts to the husband upon marriage.
4
Identify the intra-Hanafi alternative
The commentary mentions a narration from al-Khassāf and al-Hasan that divides the maintenance into thirds: two-thirds on the father, one-third on the mother, provided neither has personal wealth. This differs from the ruling for minors, where the father bears full cost due to his guardianship.
The alternative is based on the absence of guardianship over adults, thus the mother also shares.
5
Evaluate the tarjih (preference)
The commentator defends the zāhir al-riwāyah position by citing the Quranic phrase 'wa 'alā al-mawlūdi lahu' with a lām of specification, which attributes the child exclusively to the father. This specification, he argues, makes maintenance the father's sole responsibility, just as it is for minors.
This shows how a subtle linguistic point in the Quran carries legal weight and resolves the dispute.

Book of Divorce: Maintenance of Relatives. And she (the mother) is more entitled than a stranger unless she demands an increased wage. And the maintenance of an adult daughter and a disabled son is specifically upon the father; with this fatwa is given. And hiring for breastfeeding his son from another woman is valid, whether the hired woman is in his marriage, or in the waiting period, or after the waiting period. (1) (And she): meaning the mother is more entitled than a stranger unless she demands an increased wage. And maintenance of an adult daughter and a disabled son is specifically upon the father; with this fatwa is given. [1] His saying: 'whether' – this generality pertains to the second hiring, i.e. whether the woman he hired is his wife, or in the waiting period of a revocable or irrevocable divorce, or her waiting period has expired; because she is not obligated to breastfeed the son of the husband from another wife, so it is permissible to hire her for that in any case, unlike breastfeeding his son from her. (2) His saying: 'more entitled' – meaning the mother of the child who is presented to breastfeed her child from him is more entitled than a stranger to breastfeed her child; so she is given priority if she does not demand wages, or demands the like of what the stranger demands or less. But if she demands wages more than what the stranger nurse demands, then the stranger is preferable. Similarly, if the mother demands wages and the stranger volunteers without wages. All this is derived from His saying: 'A mother shall not be harmed on account of her child, nor a father on account of his child' (Quran 2:233). [3] His saying: 'unless she demands' – meaning the mother. This exception indicates that the ruling of entitlement mentioned earlier applies to the divorced mother whose waiting period has expired; because a married woman or one in waiting period cannot be hired, so there is no point in her demanding extra wages over what the stranger demands. [4] His saying: 'adult' – describing the daughter, and he indicated that femaleness is in itself a weakness, so the maintenance of a daughter is obligatory even if she is able to earn, and this is as long as she is not married; after marriage, her maintenance is upon the husband, not the father. [0] His saying: 'disabled' – with fat-ha on the zāy and kasra on the mīm, meaning one who has a chronic disability; and it is said it means one who has an illness that prevents earning, like blindness or paralysis. As in al-Kifāyah. (1) Because it is not obligatory for them to breastfeed religiously. See Majma' al-Anhur (1:498). (2) Quran 2:233. [Page 572] 'And upon the affluent.' He only said this; because according to the narration of al-Khassāf and al-Hasan, it is obligatory in thirds: two-thirds on the father and one-third on the mother; this is if they have no wealth; if they have wealth, then the maintenance is from their wealth. ('And upon the affluent') [2] [1] His saying: 'it is obligatory' – meaning the maintenance of an adult daughter and an adult disabled son is obligatory to the extent of one-third on the mother and two-thirds on the father, unlike the maintenance of minors which is solely on the father. The distinction is that the father has guardianship and expense over the minor; therefore the sadaqat al-fitr of the minor child is wajib specifically on him, and likewise maintenance; but not so for the adult because guardianship is absent, so the mother also shares. (1) (2) And the basis of the narration that the author mentioned and gave fatwa on, which is the apparent narration (zāhir al-riwāyah), is His saying: 'and upon the father' (wa 'alā al-mawlūdi lahu), with the addition of the child to the father with the lām of specification, indicates his specific relationship with this attribution, and maintenance is based on this attribution, so the mother does not share, just as she does not share in the maintenance of minors. As in al-Bināyah. [2] His saying: 'and upon the affluent (yassār al-fitra)' – meaning the one who has wealth that obligates upon him sadaqat al-fitr. So his saying 'yassār al-fitra' is in the accusative case due to removal of the preposition; i.e. like the wealth considered in its obligation, which is that he owns a nisāb surplus beyond his basic needs even if it is not growing. This is the yusr that obligates udhiyah and prohibits taking zakāh, but does not obligate giving zakāh, because for its obligation the nisāb must be growing, actually or effectively. The detail of this discussion has passed in the Book of Zakāh. And that this yusr which obligates sadaqat al-fitr and the like is considered in the obligation of maintenance of ascendants and relatives is one of the sayings here, and it is the one mentioned in al-Hidāyah and others, and he corrected it in al-Dhakhīrah, and the author of al-Bahr preferred it.
Source pages p. 571

Commentary
This passage from 'Umdat al-Ri'āyah is a commentary on the text of al-Wiqāyah, dealing with maintenance of relatives. The matn states that the mother is more entitled than a stranger to nurse her child unless she demands a higher wage. The commentary clarifies that this ruling applies only to the divorced mother whose waiting period has expired; a married or waiting-period mother cannot be hired at all. The Quranic basis is the prohibition of harming parents through nursing disputes (2:233). The matn also states that the maintenance of an adult daughter and a disabled son is solely upon the father, and this is the relied-upon fatwa. The commentary explains that the daughter's maintenance is obligatory even if she can earn because femaleness is considered a disability; after marriage it shifts to the husband. For the disabled son, the father bears the cost. However, a different narration from al-Khassāf and al-Hasan holds that maintenance of these relatives is divided into thirds: two-thirds on father, one-third on mother, unless they have their own wealth. The commentator defends the author's choice of the first view (zāhir al-riwāyah) by citing the Quranic phrase 'and upon the father' which specifies the father uniquely. The section ends with a discussion of what constitutes 'yassār al-fitra' (wealth that obligates fitr) and its application to maintenance obligations, noting that the correct view is that the same standard of affluence (ownership of a non-growing nisāb surplus) applies.

Key Terms
الأم (al-umm): The mother who is entitled to nurse her child unless she demands excessive wages.
الابن الزمن (al-ibn al-zamin): An adult son who is chronically disabled, unable to earn due to illness like blindness or paralysis.
الموسر (al-mūsir): One who possesses yassār al-fitra: wealth sufficient to obligate sadaqat al-fitr, i.e. a nisāb surplus beyond basic needs.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the relied-upon Hanafi position, who is responsible for the maintenance of an adult daughter who is not married?
A) Both parents equally
B) The father alone
C) The mother alone
D) The daughter herself

Key Takeaway
The mother's nursing priority depends on fair wages, and the father alone bears maintenance of an adult unmarried daughter and disabled son, per the relied-upon Hanafi view.

The Measure of Wealth (Yasar) for Nafaqah of Relatives
Discussion of the measure of yasar for nafaqah obligations

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the preferred Hanafi opinion on yasar for nafaqah and explain why surplus after personal expenses is the measure rather than the nisab of zakat.

Core Idea
For nafaqah, yasar means surplus after needs, not nisab; the basis is capability, not a fixed threshold.

This passage presents three opinions within the Hanafi school on what level of wealth obligates a person to support their needy relatives. The second opinion equates wealth with the nisab of zakat, while the third—and preferred—view defines it as having surplus after one's own and one's family's basic expenses. Which view is stronger and why? Let's examine the reasoning and the textual evidence.

Guided Path
1
Identify the opinions
Recognize that the passage discusses three opinions, though only the second and third are explicitly detailed. The second opinion equates yasar with owning the nisab of zakat; the third defines yasar as surplus after personal and family expenses.
The first opinion is not mentioned but implied.
2
Analyze the second opinion
Note the supporters (al-Walwalji and the author of al-Khulasa) and their evidence: analogy to zakat where nisab is the threshold for obligation.
3
Analyze the third opinion
Examine the definition from Imam Muhammad: for landowners (ahl al-ghalla), surplus sufficient for a month; for craftsmen (ahl al-hiraf), surplus sufficient for a day. Understand the reasoning: capability (qudra) matters in rights of people, not an abstract threshold like nisab.
4
Evaluate the evidence
Consider the rational proof (rights of people depend on actual ability) and the hadith threat against withholding surplus from relatives. Determine how these support the third opinion.
5
Determine the tarjih
Identify the preferred position: al-Zayla'i, the author of Fath al-Qadir, and others prefer the third opinion because it aligns with the nature of obligations toward others (based on need and surplus).
Practical consequence: a person with surplus but less than nisab is still obligated.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
يسار الفطرة يسار الفطرة ) والقول الثاني : إن المعتبر فيه كونه مالكاً لنصاب الزكاة، واختاره الولوالجي في «فتاواه»، وقال في «الخلاصة»: به نفتي. والقول الثالث : ما روي عن محمد الله أنه قدَّر بما يفضل عن نفقة نفسه وعياله شهراً إن كان من أهل الغلّة، وإن كان من أهل الحرف فهو مقدر بما يفضلُ عن نفقتِهِ ونفقة عياله كل يوم، ورجحه الزيلعي في شرح الكنز ) معللاً بأن المعتبر في حقوق العباد القدرة دون النصاب، وهو مستغن عمّا زاد على ذلك، فيصرفه إلى أقاربه، ورجحه أيضاً صاحب «الفتح» وغيره. ويؤيده حديث: «ما من ذي رحم يأتي ذوي رحمه فيسأله فضلاً أعطاه الله إياه فيبخل عليه إلا أخرج الله له من جهنّم حيّة يقال لها : شجاع، يتلمّظ فيطوق به ) أخرجه الطبراني في «المعجم الأوسط» و«الكبير» بإسناد جيد .
Fitrah wealth, fitrah wealth. The second opinion: that the consideration in it is being the owner of the nisab of zakat; al-Walwalji chose it in his Fatawa, and it is said in al-Khulasa: we give fatwa by it. The third opinion: what is narrated from Muhammad that he estimated it by what remains after his own and his family's expenses for a month if he is among the people of produce, and if he is among the people of crafts, it is estimated by what remains after his daily expenses and his family's expenses. Al-Zayla'i preferred it in Sharh al-Kanz, reasoning that in the rights of people, capability is considered, not nisab, and he is independent of what exceeds that, so he spends it on his relatives. The author of al-Fath and others also preferred it. And it is supported by the hadith: 'There is no relative who comes to his relative asking for surplus that Allah has given him, and he withholds it from him, except that Allah will bring out for him from Hellfire a snake called Shuja, licking its lips, and will be collared with it.' al-Tabarani narrated it in al-Mu'jam al-Awsat and al-Kabir with a good chain.
Source pages p. 573

Commentary
This passage is an intra-Hanafi dispute about the standard of wealth (yasar) that obligates one to support needy relatives. The second opinion equates yasar with owning the nisab of zakat (approx. 85g gold). The third opinion, from Imam Muhammad, measures yasar by having surplus after one's own and family's basic needs for a month (for farmers/landowners) or daily (for craftsmen). The commentator prefers the third opinion, arguing that capability (qudra) is what matters in rights of people, not abstract nisab. He supports this with a stern hadith threatening a withholding relative with a hellish snake. The first opinion (missing) likely defined yasar differently. This preference is also adopted by al-Zayla'i and the author of Fath al-Qadir.

Key Terms
يسار (yasar): Wealth or financial capacity sufficient to incur the obligation of supporting relatives.
نصاب الزكاة (nisab al-zakat): The minimum wealth threshold that makes zakat obligatory (e.g., 85g gold or equivalent).

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the preferred opinion in this passage, what is the measure of wealth (yasar) for obligation of nafaqah?
A) Owning the nisab of zakat
B) Having surplus after one's own and family's basic expenses
C) Being able to earn an income
D) Being free from debt

Key Takeaway
The Hanafi preference for the third opinion on yasar emphasizes capability over fixed thresholds, ensuring that obligation arises from actual surplus, not mere possession of nisab.

Maintenance of Poor Ascendants: Conditions and Proof
Explains the obligation of nafaqah for poor ascendants upon wealthy descendants equally.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the two conditions for the obligation of nafaqah for ascendants in the Hanafi school and apply them to determine who must support whom.

Core Idea
Wealthy descendants must support poor ascendants equally; kindness requires preventing starvation.

This passage from al-Bahr al-Ra'iq explains the Hanafi ruling on maintenance of ascendants (usul). It clarifies that the obligation is wajib upon all wealthy descendants, male and female, provided the ascendant is poor. The proof is derived from the Quranic command to accompany parents with kindness (ma'ruf). Understanding the conditions and the equal distribution is crucial for correctly applying the ruling in family maintenance cases.

Guided Path
1
Identify the act and ruling
The act is nafaqah (maintenance) for poor ascendants. The hukm is wajib upon wealthy descendants.
The ruling is not fard because the dalil is zanni al-dalala.
2
Define the key terms
Understand 'usul' (ascendants) and 'bil-sawiyyah' (equally). Usul includes all ancestors, maternal and paternal. Bil-sawiyyah means the obligation is shared among all wealthy descendants without gender distinction.
This differs from inheritance rules where sons get double.
3
State the conditions for obligation
Two conditions: (1) the ascendant must be poor (faqir) — even if able to earn; (2) the descendant must be wealthy (musir) — having surplus beyond own family needs.
A poor person is never obligated except for spouse and young child.
4
Examine the dalil
The proof is Quran 31:15: 'And accompany them in the world with kindness.' The wajh al-dalalah is that kindness includes preventing starvation, so maintenance is wajib.
The dalil is qati' al-thubut but zanni al-dalala, hence the ruling is wajib not fard.
5
Note cross-madhhab difference
The Hanafi school extends the obligation to all ascendants. Some Shafi'is restrict it to parents only, based on a narrower interpretation of the verse.
The practical effect: Hanafis require supporting grandparents; Shafi'is do not.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
لا المعسر نفقة أصوله الفقراء بالسوية [1] قوله : أصوله ؛ كالام وأم الأم وإن علت، والأب وأب الأب وإن علا، وأب الأم، والجدة الفاسدة، ويستثنى منه الأمّ المتزوّجة وغيرها، فإن نفقتها على زوجها، كالبنت المراهقة إذا زوّجها أبوها فإنّ نفقتها على زوجها لا على أبيها. كذا في «البحر». أمران : [٢]قوله : الفقراء؛ صفة للأصول ؛ والحاصل أنه يعتبر في وجوب نفقة الأصول أحدهم : كون من تجب نفقته فقيراً، وإن كان قادراً على الكسب، فإنه لو كان ذا مال فنفقته في ماله ولا تجب نفقةُ . موسر على أحد إلا الزوجة الموسرة تجب نفقتها على الزوج، جزاء للاحتباس، وأما نفقةً غيرها فإنّما تجب للصلة، ولا وجوب للصلة إلا عند الاحتياج، وهو بالفقر. والأصل فيه قوله : وَصَاحِبَهُمَا فِي الدُّنْيَا مَعْرُوفًا : أي الوالدين، ويلحق بهما جميع الأصول، وليس من المعروف أن يموت أحد من الأصول جوعاً وهو يعيش في نعم الله الله. وثانيهما : كونُ مَن تجب عليه النفقةُ موسراً ، فإنّ الفقير محتاج إلى غيره ، فكيف تجب عليه نفقة غيره ولا تجب على الفقير نفقةُ أحدٍ إلا الزوجة والطفل الصغير كما مرّ ذكره [٣]قوله : بالسوية ؛ أي وجوب نفقة الأصول على الفروع الأغنياء على الاستواء من غير تفرقة بين الذكر والأنثى، ففي من له بنت وابن نفقته عليهما على التناصف.
Not the destitute; maintenance of his poor ascendants equally. [1] His statement: 'his ascendants' — like the mother and the mother of the mother even if high, and the father and the father of the father even if high, and the maternal grandfather, and the grandmother from a false lineage, but excluded is the married mother and others, for her maintenance is on her husband, like the adolescent daughter if her father marries her off, her maintenance is on her husband, not on her father. Thus in al-Bahr. Two matters: [2] His statement: 'the poor' — an adjective for the ascendants; the conclusion is that in the obligation of maintenance of ascendants, two conditions are considered: first, that the one whose maintenance is due is poor, even if he is capable of earning, for if he has wealth, his maintenance is from his own wealth, and maintenance is not obligatory upon a wealthy person for anyone except the wealthy wife — her maintenance is obligatory upon her husband as a recompense for confinement. As for the maintenance of others, it is obligatory only for connection (silat), and connection is not obligatory except in need, which is poverty. The basis for this is His statement: 'And accompany them in the world with kindness' — meaning the parents, and all ascendants are included in this. It is not kindness that one of the ascendants dies of hunger while he lives in Allah's bounties. Second, that the one upon whom maintenance is obligatory is wealthy, for the poor is in need of others, so how can maintenance of another be obligatory upon him? And maintenance of anyone is not obligatory upon a poor person except the wife and the young child, as previously mentioned. [3] His statement: 'equally' — meaning the obligation of maintenance of ascendants upon wealthy descendants is equal without distinction between male and female. So, for one who has a daughter and a son, his maintenance is upon them equally.
Source pages p. 574

Commentary
This passage is a ruling with proof concerning the obligation of maintaining ascendants (usul). It comments on the matn: 'Not the destitute; maintenance of his poor ascendants equally.' First, it defines ascendants: all ancestors, including maternal and paternal lines, except a married mother whose husband is responsible. Second, it lays down two conditions: (i) the ascendant must be poor — even if able to earn, if no wealth, the descendant owes maintenance; (ii) the descendant must be wealthy — a poor person cannot be liable for others except his wife and young child. The proof is the Quranic command to treat parents with kindness, which logically requires preventing their starvation. Third, it clarifies that the obligation is shared equally among all wealthy descendants, male and female. So if a man has a son and a daughter, they split the maintenance equally.

Key Terms
أصول (usul): Ascendants: parents and all ancestors in the maternal and paternal lines.
بالسوية (bil-sawiyyah): Equally, meaning all wealthy descendants share the obligation proportionally.
موسر (musir): Wealthy: one who has surplus beyond his own and his family's needs.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint

A) The descendant must have more than the nisab of zakat
B) The descendant must be wealthy and the ascendant poor
C) The ascendant must be unable to earn
D) The descendant must be a son

Key Takeaway
Maintenance of poor ascendants is a wajib obligation upon all wealthy descendants, shared equally regardless of gender.

Nafaqah — Maintenance
