Maintenance of Poor Ascendants: Obligation and Equal Distribution
Sharh on obligation and equal distribution of nafaqah for ascendants

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the conditions for the obligation of nafaqah on wealthy descendants for poor ascendants, and apply the rule of equal distribution based on closeness and lineage.

Core Idea
Obligation to support poor ascendants is equal among descendants, based on closeness and lineage, not inheritance shares.

This passage from 'Umdat al-Ri'ayah expands on the Hanafi ruling that wealthy descendants must provide maintenance (nafaqah) for their poor ascendants. The commentary clarifies the scope of 'ascendants', the conditions of poverty and wealth, and crucially, that the obligation is divided equally among all descendants—male and female—based on their closeness of lineage (qurb) and the direction of birth (juz'iyyah), not on how they would inherit. This lesson will walk you through the legal reasoning and the key examples that illustrate this principle.

Guided Path
1
Define the scope of 'ascendants'
Identify who is included as an ascendant: parents, grandparents (including irregular grandmothers), and all ancestors upward. Note the exception for married mothers and married daughters whose nafaqah is on their husbands.
The exception shows that the obligation on the descendant is secondary to a closer obligation (the husband's).
2
Identify the two conditions for obligation
(1) The ascendant must be poor (even if capable of earning). (2) The descendant must be wealthy (maysir). Understand that a poor descendant is not obligated except for wife and minor child.
The sole evidence cited is Quran 31:15, interpreted as a command of kindness including financial support in need.
3
Understand the principle of equal distribution
The nafaqah is wajib 'bis sawiyyah' equally on all descendants, male and female. The distribution is based on closeness and partiality (juz'iyyah), not on inheritance shares.
This is a distinctive Hanafi position: gender equality in obligation.
4
Apply the principle to examples
Work through the given cases: daughter vs. grandson (son's son) → all on daughter; daughter's child vs. brother → all on daughter's child; son vs. grandson → all on son; two sons (one Muslim, one Christian or female) → equal. Verify how closeness and juz'iyyah determine the distribution.
Note that inheritance shares would give different results; the text explicitly distinguishes.
5
Reinforce the basis: juz'iyyah then qurb
The obligation is proportional to lineage connection (juz'iyyah), and then the closest takes precedence. Being an heir or not is irrelevant.
This is a key usul point: the 'illah (effective cause) is the lineage connection, not the inheritance relationship.

Not the poor (have to provide) maintenance for his ascendants who are poor equally. And in al-Misbah al-Munir: 'Their statement: Fitrah is obligatory... the original is that Zakat al-Fitrah is obligatory, and it is the body, so the addendum is omitted and the annex is added in its place, and it is used sufficiently for understanding the meaning.' (1) (1) His statement: his ascendants; like the mother and the mother's mother even if high, and the father and the father's father even if high, and the father's mother, and the irregular grandmother, and from that is excluded the married mother and others, for her maintenance is upon her husband, like the adolescent daughter if her father marries her off, her maintenance is upon her husband, not upon her father. Thus in al-Bahr. Two matters: [2] His statement: the poor; an adjective for the ascendants; and the conclusion is that in the obligation of maintenance of ascendants, two conditions are considered: One: that the person whose maintenance is obligatory is poor, even if he is capable of earning, for if he were wealthy, his maintenance would be on his own wealth, and the maintenance of a wealthy person is not obligatory upon anyone except the wealthy wife, her maintenance is obligatory upon the husband as a recompense for confinement. As for maintenance of others, it is only obligatory for connection (silah), and connection is only obligatory in need, which is poverty. The basis for this is His statement: 'And accompany them in this world with kindness' (Quran 31:15), i.e., the parents, and all ascendants are joined to them, and it is not from kindness that one of the ascendants dies of hunger while he lives in Allah's blessings. And the second: that the person upon whom maintenance is obligatory is wealthy, for the poor person is in need of others, so how can the maintenance of others be obligatory upon him? And maintenance of anyone is not obligatory upon the poor except the wife and the young child, as previously mentioned. [3] His statement: equally; i.e., the obligation of maintenance of ascendants upon wealthy descendants is equally, without distinction between male and female. So for one who has a daughter and a son, his maintenance is upon both in halves (tasaf). Between the son and the daughter, consideration is made for closeness and partiality (juz'iyyah), not inheritance. So for one who has a daughter and a grandson (son's son), it is all upon the daughter. And for one who has a daughter's child and a brother, maintenance is upon the daughter's child. While inheritance is halves between the daughter and grandson, and all the inheritance is for the brother, and nothing for the daughter's child because he is from dhawi al-arham. [1] His statement: and consideration is made; i.e., what is considered in the maintenance of ascendants is closeness after partiality, without consideration of whether the obligated person is an heir. Meaning, first partiality is considered, i.e., the direction of birth, then the closest is given priority, without looking at whether he is an heir or not. That is because the obligation of this maintenance is proportional to partiality, so it has consideration. And closeness is considered to give priority to the more complete over the less complete. So for two sons, one Muslim and one Christian or female, his maintenance is upon both equally due to equality in closeness and partiality, even if the Christian is deprived of inheritance from his Muslim father and the female takes half of what the male takes. And for a son and a grandson (son's son), it is upon the son only due to his closeness. And for a daughter and a grandson, it is upon the daughter only due to closeness. And for a grandson and a granddaughter (daughter's daughter), it is upon them equally. Thus in Fath al-Qadir and others. (2) His statement: while... etc.; its summary: if a man died leaving a daughter and a grandson (son's son), the wealth is between them in halves, half for the daughter by way of fard (prescribed share) and the remainder for the grandson by way of 'asabah (residuaries). So if inheritance were considered, the maintenance of the father would be upon them equally. Similarly, if a man leaves his brother and a daughter's daughter or daughter's son, all the wealth is for the brother because he is an 'asabah if he is a full or consanguine brother, and if he is a uterine brother, he gets one-sixth by fard and the remainder is returned to him, and nothing is for the children of the daughter who are from dhawi al-arham in the presence of 'asabat or owners of prescribed shares. So if inheritance were considered, the maintenance would be upon the brother, not upon the daughter's child. [3] His statement: because; i.e., the daughter's child, male or female, is from dhawi al-arham, and they are relatives who have no prescribed shares in the Shari'ah, nor do they take the remainder after giving the prescribed shares, or all when alone by way of 'asabah.
Source pages p. 574

Commentary
This passage is an expansion (sharh) from 'Umdat al-Ri'ayah on the ruling of maintenance (nafaqah) for ascendants (usul) from the matn of al-Wiqayah. The author begins by clarifying the phrase 'his ascendants' (usuluhu), listing who is included: mother, grandmothers, father, grandfathers, father's mother, and the so-called irregular grandmother (al-jaddah al-fasidah, which is a grandmother related through a male who is not a direct line, e.g., mother's father's mother). An exception is the married mother or a daughter who is married; their maintenance is on their husbands, not on the descendant. He cites al-Bahr for this. Then he discusses two conditions (amrani) for the obligation: First, the ascendant must be poor, even if able to earn, because if wealthy, their maintenance is on their own wealth. The only wealthy person whose maintenance is obligatory on another is the wealthy wife, due to the confinement (ihtibas) of marriage. For others, maintenance is for the sake of connection (sillah), which is only obligatory in need (poverty). The primary evidence is Quran 31:15, 'wa sahibhuma fi al-dunya ma'rufa' – accompany them in this world with kindness. This is interpreted as a command of birr, which includes financial support. The author stresses that it is not from kindness to let ascendants die of hunger while the descendant lives in blessings. Second, the descendant must be wealthy, because a poor person cannot be obligated to support others; only a wife and minor child can be supported by a poor person (as previously established). Then he explains the equality (bis sawiyyah): the obligation is equally upon all descendants, male and female, without discrimination. For example, if someone has a son and a daughter, the maintenance is on both equally (tanasuf). The basis for distribution is closeness (qurb) and partiality (juz'iyyah, i.e., being from the same lineage), not inheritance (irth). He gives examples: if one has a daughter and a grandson (son's son), the entire maintenance is on the daughter because she is closer. If one has a daughter's child and a brother, the maintenance is on the daughter's child, even though in inheritance the daughter's child (being from dhawi al-arham) gets nothing and the brother gets everything. Similarly, for a son and a grandson, the son bears the whole maintenance due to his closeness. But if the descendants are equal in closeness (like two sons, one Muslim and one Christian, or a male and female), they share equally. The author notes that this is the position in Fath al-Qadir and others. He further explains that partiality (juz'iyyah) is the primary consideration, then closeness; the fact that one is an heir or not is irrelevant because the obligation is proportional to lineage. Thus, the ruling is clear: wealthy descendants must support their poor ascendants equally, regardless of gender or religion, based on closeness and lineage, not on shares of inheritance.

Key Terms
الأصول (al-usul): Ascendants: parents, grandparents, and all ancestors upward, including irregular grandmothers (al-jaddah al-fasidah).
بالسوية (bis sawiyyah): Equally: the obligation of nafaqah is shared equally among descendants (male and female), without differentiation.
الجزئية (al-juz'iyyah): Partiality or lineage connection: the fact of being born from the person (direction of birth) which is the basis for the obligation.
ذوي الأرحام (dhawi al-arham): Uterine relatives who are not entitled to fixed shares or residuary in inheritance; they are not 'asabat nor sahib al-fard.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the Hanafi position in this passage, what is the basis for distributing the obligation of nafaqah of ascendants among descendants?
A) Division according to inheritance shares
B) Equality among all descendants, considering closeness and lineage
C) Only male descendants are obligated
D) Only the eldest descendant is obligated

Key Takeaway
Wealthy descendants must support their poor ascendants equally, based on closeness of lineage, not on inheritance shares.

Nafaqah — Maintenance
intermediate
10 min
Maintenance of Mahram Relatives: Obligation and Amount
Explaining the basis and scope of maintenance for mahram relatives

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi ruling on maintenance of mahram relatives, identify the conditions that trigger the obligation, and apply the principle that the amount is proportional to the inheritance share.

Core Idea
Maintenance of mahram relatives is based on closeness and partiality, not inheritance; the amount follows the inheritance proportion.

The maintenance of relatives is a financial obligation in Hanafi fiqh, but it is not arbitrary. This lesson explains two key dimensions: for ascendants (parents), the obligation is determined by closeness (qurb) and partiality (juziyya) regardless of inheritance rights; for other mahram relatives, the obligation arises when they are in need and the amount is directly tied to the share they would inherit. We will walk through the textual proofs and conditions from the classical Hanafi texts.

Guided Path
1
Distinguish ascendants from other mahram relatives
The passage first discusses maintenance of ascendants (parents/grandparents) where the key factors are closeness and partiality, not inheritance. Then it discusses other mahram relatives (siblings, uncles, etc.) where conditions of need apply and the amount is based on inheritance share.
The ruling for parents is broader: even if they can earn, maintenance is wajib.
2
For ascendants: apply partiality and closeness
Partiality (juziyya) means direct blood line (child). Closeness (qurb) means the nearest relative. In the examples, a daughter is preferred over a son's son because she is closer, even though the son's son might inherit more.
The ruling is illustrated with scenarios where inheritance differs, but maintenance follows closeness.
3
For other mahram relatives: identify the conditions
Maintenance is wajib only if the relative is poor, minor, adult female, disabled (zamanah), or blind. These are signs of inability to earn. The obligated person must be financially capable (musir).
Parents are an exception: even if they can earn, maintenance is wajib.
4
Understand the proportional amount rule
The amount of maintenance for non-ascendant mahram relatives is 'on the proportion of inheritance' based on Quran 2:233. This means if the relative would inherit 1/4, the obligated person must provide 1/4 of the needed maintenance.
This is a unique Hanafi position linking maintenance to hypothetical inheritance.
5
Apply to scenarios
Use the rules to determine who is obligated and how much. For example, a blind brother gets maintenance proportional to his inheritance share from the obligated sibling.
The text explicitly contrasts with inheritance: closeness matters, not actual inheritance rights.

[٣] قوله : زَمِن؛ - بفتح الزاي المعجمة وكسر الميم - ؛ أي من به زمانة، والمراد بها فقد اليدين والرجلين معاً، أو اليدين فقط ، أو الرجلين فقط ، أو رجـل ويـد مـن جانب واحد.
[٤]قوله : على قدر الإرث ؛ يعني وجوب نفقة المحارم ذوي الرحم غير الأصول على قدر الإرث ؛ لقوله : وَعَلَى الْوَارِثِ مِثْلُ ذَلِكَ (۲) ؛ أي مثلُ النفقة التي وجبت
Between the son and the daughter, and consideration is given therein to closeness and partiality, not inheritance. Thus, for one who has a daughter and a son's son, all [maintenance] is upon the daughter. And for the child of a daughter and a brother, [maintenance is] upon her child. Between the son and the daughter, consideration is given to closeness and partiality, not inheritance. So for one who has a daughter and a son's son, all is upon the daughter. And for the child of a daughter and a brother, [it is] upon her child, even though inheritance is half between the daughter and the son's son, and all inheritance is for the brother, and nothing for the child of the daughter because he is from the dhawu al-arham.
[1] His saying: 'and consideration is given'; meaning: what is considered in the maintenance of ascendants is closeness after partiality, without [regard to] whether the one upon whom it is obligatory is an heir. That is, partiality – meaning the relationship of birth – is considered first, then the closest is given precedence over the next closest, without regard to whether he is an heir or not. This is because the obligation of this maintenance is in proportion to partiality, so it is given consideration. And closeness is considered to give precedence to the more complete over the less complete. Thus, for two children, one of whom is Muslim and the other a Christian or a female, their maintenance is obligatory upon both equally due to equality in closeness and partiality, even though the Christian is deprived of inheriting from his Muslim father, and the female takes half of what the male takes. And for a son and a son's son, [maintenance] is upon the son only due to his closeness. And for a daughter and a son's son, [it is] upon the daughter only due to closeness. And for a son's son and a daughter's daughter, [it is] equally. As in 'Fath al-Qadir' and others.
(2) His saying: 'even though...' etc.; its summary: If a man dies leaving a daughter and a son's son, the wealth is half between them: half for the daughter as a prescribed share, and the remainder for the son's son as a residuary. So if inheritance were considered, the maintenance of the father would be upon both equally. Similarly, if a man leaves his brother and a daughter's daughter or a daughter's son, all the wealth is for the brother because he is a residuary if [the brother] is from the father and mother or from the father, and if from the mother, then one-sixth is for him as a prescribed share, and the remainder is returned to him, and nothing is for the children of the daughter who are from the dhawu al-arham when residuaries or prescribed sharers are present. So if inheritance were considered, maintenance would be upon the brother, not upon the daughter's child. [3] His saying: 'because he'; i.e., the child of the daughter, male or female, is from the dhawu al-arham, and they are the relatives who have no prescribed shares in the Sharia, nor do they take the remainder after giving the prescribed shares, nor all when alone as residuaries.

And the maintenance of every mahram relative who is a minor and poor, or an adult female who is poor, or a disabled male, or a blind [person], is according to the proportion of inheritance.
[4] His saying: 'and the maintenance of every mahram relative blind according to the proportion of inheritance' [is part of the text].
[1] His saying: 'and maintenance'; it is conjoined to his saying: 'maintenance of his ascendants'; i.e., upon the person at the level of fitra affluence is the maintenance of every dhi rahm, i.e., a mahram relative – and mahram (with fath on the mim) is one whose marriage is perpetually unlawful. He indicated by mentioning the two conditions that maintenance is not obligatory for a non-mahram relative, like the cousin [ibn al-amm], nor for a mahram who is not a relative, like the mother of the wife or a foster brother. As in 'al-Binaya'. Then the meaning of mahram is one whose mahram status is due to kinship, not due to another reason. Thus, if the cousin is a foster brother, his maintenance is not obligatory because although he is true as a mahram relative, his mahram status is due to an accidental cause of fosterage, not to his kinship.
[2] His saying: 'minor poor... etc.'; the conclusion is that maintenance of a mahram relative is not obligatory upon the affluent except when he is in need of it, and that occurs through poverty, minority, femininity, disability, and blindness, for these are signs of inability. Thus, maintenance is not obligatory for a male capable of earning, unlike the parents, for it is obligatory to spend on them when they are poor even if they are capable of earning, because the hardship of earning befalls them, and the child is commanded to repel harm from them, so their maintenance is obligatory. This is not the case for other relatives. As in 'al-Hidayah' and its glosses.
[3] His saying: 'disabled' (zamin) – with fatha on the zay and kasra on the mim – i.e., one who has a disability (zamana), meaning loss of hands and feet together, or only hands, or only feet, or one foot and one hand on one side.
[4] His saying: 'according to the proportion of inheritance'; meaning the obligation of maintenance for mahram relatives other than ascendants is according to the proportion of inheritance, because of His saying: 'And upon the heir is like that' (Quran 2:233); i.e., like the maintenance that was obligated.
Source pages p. 575

Commentary
This passage is an expansion on the rulings of maintenance for relatives. It begins by establishing the principle that in determining who bears the maintenance of ascendants (such as parents), the key factors are closeness (qurb) and partiality (juziyya), not inheritance (irth). Partiality refers to the direct blood tie (walad), and then the closest relative is prioritized even if that relative does not inherit. The author gives examples: if a man has a daughter and a son's son, the maintenance of the parent falls solely on the daughter because she is closer (direct child) than the son's son (a grandchild). Similarly, between the child of a daughter and a brother, the maintenance is on the child of the daughter because she is a closer descendant, even though in inheritance the brother takes everything and the daughter's child gets nothing (being a dhu rahm). The commentary emphasizes that the obligation is based on the degree of blood relation, not on being an heir. 

The second part addresses the maintenance of other mahram relatives (non-ascendants). According to Hanafi fiqh, maintenance is wajib for every mahram relative (one who is permanently forbidden in marriage due to kinship) who is poor, minor, an adult female, disabled, or blind, provided the obligated person (the nafaqa giver) is financially capable (musir, i.e., possesses nisab or surplus). The amount of maintenance is proportional to the share of inheritance that relative would receive if the nafaqa giver were to die. This is based on the Quranic verse: 'And upon the heir is like that' (Al-Baqarah 2:233). The commentary clarifies that 'mahram' here means only kinship-based mahrams, not those who become mahram through fosterage or marriage. Also, parents are excepted: their maintenance is wajib even if they are capable of earning, due to the respect of parents and the command to avoid harm to them. For other relatives, maintenance is only due if they are unable to earn due to age, gender, or disability. The examples illustrate the principle of closeness and partiality, and the proportional obligation.

Key Terms
محرم (mahram): A relative with whom marriage is permanently forbidden due to blood relation (nasab), e.g., brother, uncle, etc. Excludes those who become mahram through fosterage or marriage.
قرب (qurb): Closeness in blood relation; in maintenance, the closest relative is given priority over a more distant one.
جزئية (juziyya): Partiality: the direct blood line (walad) that makes one a part of the person; e.g., children are a part of their parents.
زمانة (zamānah): Chronic disability: loss of hands, feet, or both, making the person unable to earn.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the Hanafi school, the maintenance of a mahram relative (non-ascendant) is wajib on a wealthy person only if the relative is:
A) An adult male capable of earning
B) Poor, minor, female, disabled, or blind
C) Only a minor child
D) Only a parent

Key Takeaway
The Hanafi school bases maintenance of mahram relatives on closeness and partiality for ascendants and on need plus inheritance proportion for others, making it a precise financial duty.

Nafaqah — Maintenance
intermediate
10 min
Maintenance of Mahram Relatives Based on Inheritance Capacity
Commentary on the rule and rationale for maintenance of mahram relatives

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the conditions under which maintenance of a mahram relative is wajib and explain why potential inheritance (ahliyyat al-irth) is the criterion.

Core Idea
Maintenance of a mahram relative is wajib based on need and potential inheritance, not actual inheritance.

The Hanafi school derives the obligation to support needy mahram relatives from the Qur'anic verse 'And upon the inheritor is the like of that.' This commentary from 'Umda al-Ri'aya clarifies which relatives are covered, when maintenance is required, and how the amount is determined by potential inheritance shares.

Guided Path
1
Identify the act and its ruling
Determine what action is being ruled upon and its legal classification. Here, the act is providing maintenance (nafaqah) to certain relatives, and the ruling is wajib (obligatory).
The obligation is conditional; not all relatives qualify.
2
List the conditions that trigger the obligation
The passage specifies that the relative must be a mahram by blood, and must be in need due to childhood, poverty (for a female adult), chronic disability (zamanah), or blindness. The supporter must also be financially capable (musir).
Need is indicated by these specific signs of incapacity.
3
Understand the scope of 'mahram'
Mahram here is restricted to blood relationship (nasab). Relatives by marriage or fosterage, even if otherwise unmarriageable, are not included. Also, non-mahram blood relatives like cousins (ibn amm) are excluded.
The two restrictions: blood relative + mahram.
4
Analyze the proof from the Quran
The ruling is based on the verse 'And upon the inheritor is the like of that' (2:233). The Hanafi school interprets 'inheritor' to include those with potential to inherit (ahliyyat al-irth), not just actual inheritors, because actual inheritance is only known after death and cannot be the basis for a living obligation.
This is a key usul extension: from actual to potential.
5
Note the exceptional treatment of parents
Unlike other mahram relatives, parents are entitled to maintenance even if they are capable of earning, because of the special command to honor and protect parents from hardship.
This exception is from al-Hidaya.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
ونفقةُ كلِّ ذي رحم مَحْرَمٍ صغير فقير أو أنثى بالغة فقيرة، أو ذكر زمن، أو أعمى على قدر الإرث ويُجْبَرُ عليه، ويُعتبرُ فيها أهلية الإرث لا حقيقته.

ثم قوله: ونفقة؛ عطف على قوله: «نفقة أصوله»؛ أي على الموسر يسار الفطرة نفقة كل ذي رحم؛ أي قرابة محرم، وهو – بالفتح – : من لا يحل نكاحه به أبداً، وأشار بذكر القيدين إلى أنه لا تجب نفقة ذي رحم غير محرم، كابن العم، ولا نفقة محرم غير ذي رحم، كأم الزوجة والأخ الرضاعي. كذا في «البناية».
ثم المراد بالمحرم من تكون محرميّته للقرابة لا لأمر آخر، فابن العم إذا كان أخاً رضاعيّاً له لا تجب نفقته؛ لأنه وإن صدق عليه أنه ذو رحم محرم لكن محرميّته لعارض الرضاعة لا لرحمه.

قوله: صغير فقير... الخ؛ الحاصل أنه لا تجب نفقةُ ذي رحم محرم على الموسر إلا عند حاجته إليها، وهي إنّما يكون بالفقر والصغر والأنوثة والزمانة والعمى، فإنّ هذه إمارات العجز، فلا تجب نفقةُ الذكر القادرِ على الكسب.
بخلاف الأبوين، فإنّه يجب أن ينفق عليها عند فقرهما وإن كانا قادرين على الكسب؛ لأنه يلحقهما تعب الكسب، والولد مأمور بدفع الضرر عنهما، فتجب نفقتهما، ولا كذلك غيرهما من أصحاب القرابة. كذا في «الهداية» وحواشيها.

قوله: زَمِن؛ - بفتح الزاي المعجمة وكسر الميم -؛ أي من به زمانة، والمراد بها فقد اليدين والرجلين معاً، أو اليدين فقط، أو الرجلين فقط، أو رجل ويد من جانب واحد.

قوله: على قدر الإرث؛ يعني وجوب نفقة المحارم ذوي الرحم غير الأصول على قدر الإرث؛ لقوله: وَعَلَى الْوَارِثِ مِثْلُ ذَلِكَ؛ أي مثلُ النفقة التي وجبت.

ويجبر عليه، ويُعْتَبَرُ فيها أهليَّةُ الإرث لا حقيقته: وإنما قال هذا؛ لان نفقة هؤلاء إنما تجب؛ لقوله تعالى: ﴿ وَعَلَى الْوَارِثِ مِثْلُ ذَلِكَ ﴾، فينبغي أن لا تجب إلا على الوارث، فقال: المعتبر أهليَّةُ الإرث لا حقيقته، وذلك لأن حقيقةً الإرث لا تعلم إلا بعد الموت، فمن له خال وابن عم يمكن أن يموت ابن العم أولاً، ويكون الإرث للخال على المولود واجبة على الوارث، فحكم الله له بوجوب النفقة باسم الوارث، فدلّ ذلك على اعتبار الإرث في هذا الباب.

قوله: ويجبر؛ أي يجبر الموسرُ الذي تجب عليه النفقة على الإنفاق بالحبس ونحوه.

قوله: أهلية الإرث؛ احترز به عمّن كان مخالفاً لدينه، كالنصراني واليهودي، كما ستطلع عليه إن شاء الله تعالى.

قوله: فقال المعتبر ...الخ؛ يعني لما علم من الآية أن المعتبر في هذا الباب هو الإرث، ولا يمكن جعل حقيقة الإرث مناطاً، فجعلت أهلية الإرث معتبرة.

قوله: فمن له خال؛ يعني رجل موصوف بصفات توجب نفقته على غيره على ما مر له خال موسر؛ أي أخ أمه وابن عمّ تجب نفقته على الخال، فإنّه وارث في الجملة، بكونه أهلاً له، فإنّه لو مات الرجلُ وتركَ خالاً فقط، بأن مات ابن عمه قبله يرث الخال ماله، ولو مات وترك ابن عمه وخاله، فالمال كله لابن عمه؛ لأنه عصبة، فهو يحجب الخال الذي من ذوي الأرحام.

وبالجملة: فحقيقة الإرث غير مرادةٍ في الآية؛ فإن الوارث حقيقة من قام به الإرث بالفعل، وهذا لا يتحقق إلا بعد موت من تجب له النفقة، ولا نفقة بعد الموت، فكان المراد من هو أهل للإرث؛ ولذا وجبت النفقة في الصورة المذكورة على الخال.
And the maintenance of every blood relative who is a mahram - a minor poor, or an adult poor female, or a disabled male, or a blind person - is [obligatory] according to the [inheritance] share. And he is compelled to it, and consideration is given to capacity to inherit, not the actual inheritance.

Then his statement: 'And maintenance' is conjoined to his statement: 'maintenance of his ascendants'; i.e., upon the wealthy person of sound disposition is the maintenance of every blood relative, i.e., a mahram relative, and he - with fatha - is one whom it is never permissible to marry. By mentioning the two restrictions, he indicates that maintenance is not obligatory for a blood relative who is not a mahram, like the son of a paternal uncle, nor for a mahram who is not a blood relative, like the mother of the wife or a foster brother. This is from al-Binaya.
Then what is meant by mahram is one whose mahram status is due to blood relationship, not another cause. So if a son of a paternal uncle is a foster brother to him, his maintenance is not obligatory, because even though he is described as a blood relative mahram, his mahram status is due to the accident of fosterage, not his blood.

His statement: 'small, poor... etc.'; the conclusion is that maintenance of a mahram blood relative upon the wealthy is not obligatory except when there is need for it, and that is only through poverty, childhood, femininity, chronic illness, and blindness, for these are signs of incapacity. So maintenance is not obligatory for a male capable of earning.
Unlike the parents, for maintenance is obligatory upon them when they are poor even if they are capable of earning, because hardship of earning afflicts them, and the child is commanded to repel harm from them, so their maintenance is obligatory. And not so for other relatives. This is from al-Hidaya and its glosses.

His statement: 'zamin' - with fatiha on the za and kasr on the mim - i.e., one afflicted with zamana, and by it is meant loss of both hands and feet together, or both hands only, or both feet only, or one hand and one foot from one side.

His statement: 'according to the [inheritance] share'; means the obligation of maintenance of mahram blood relatives other than ascendants is according to the inheritance share, because of His statement: 'And upon the inheritor is the like of that' i.e., like the maintenance that became obligatory.

'And he is compelled to it, and consideration is given to capacity to inherit, not the actual inheritance': And he only said this because the maintenance of these people is obligatory due to His statement: 'And upon the inheritor is the like of that', so it should not be obligatory except upon the actual inheritor. So he said: 'What is considered is capacity to inherit, not actual inheritance', and that is because actual inheritance is not known except after death. So for one who has a maternal uncle and a son of a paternal uncle, it is possible that the son of the paternal uncle dies first and the inheritance is for the maternal uncle - maintenance upon the child is obligatory upon the inheritor, so Allah ruled for him the obligation of maintenance in the name of inheritor. So that indicates the consideration of inheritance in this chapter.

His statement: 'and he is compelled'; i.e., the wealthy person upon whom maintenance is obligatory is compelled to spend by imprisonment and the like.

His statement: 'capacity to inherit'; he avoided thereby one who is of a different religion, like a Christian or Jew, as you will see if Allah wills.

His statement: 'he said what is considered...etc.'; means when it was known from the verse that what is considered in this chapter is inheritance, and it is not possible to make actual inheritance the effective cause, capacity to inherit was made considered.

His statement: 'for one who has a maternal uncle'; means a man described with attributes that obligate his maintenance upon others as previously mentioned: he has a wealthy maternal uncle i.e., his mother's brother, and a son of a paternal uncle, his maintenance is obligatory upon the maternal uncle, for he is an inheritor in some measure, being qualified for it. For if the man dies leaving only a maternal uncle, with the son of the paternal uncle having died before him, the maternal uncle inherits his property. And if he dies leaving a son of a paternal uncle and a maternal uncle, all the property goes to the son of the paternal uncle because he is an asaba, so he excludes the maternal uncle who is among the dhawil-arham.

In summary: actual inheritance is not intended in the verse, for the actual inheritor is the one who actually inherits, and this is not realized except after the death of the one for whom maintenance is due, and there is no maintenance after death. So what was meant is the one who is qualified for inheritance, and therefore maintenance was obligatory in the mentioned scenario upon the maternal uncle.
Source pages p. 576

Commentary
This passage from the commentary 'Umda al-Ri'aya' explains the Hanafi ruling on maintenance (nafaqah) of blood relatives who are mahram (permanently unmarriageable). It is a ruling with proof. The core ruling: maintenance is wajib upon a wealthy person for a mahram relative who is needy due to childhood, poverty (for a female adult), chronic illness (zamanah), or blindness. The amount is according to the inheritance share the relative would potentially receive (ahliyyat al-irth), not actual inheritance. The proof is the Qur'anic verse (2:233): 'And upon the inheritor is the like of that.' The commentary clarifies that the mahram must be by blood, not marriage or fosterage. It also notes that parents are exceptional: their maintenance is wajib even if they are capable of earning, unlike other relatives. The principle of considering potential inheritance is explained with an example: if a man has a maternal uncle and a cousin (ibn amm), the wealthy maternal uncle must pay maintenance because he could inherit if the cousin dies first, even though the cousin may be the actual heir at present. The commentary emphasizes that actual inheritance cannot be the basis because maintenance is due during life, not after death. The compulsion to pay is through imprisonment or similar means. Non-Muslim relatives are excluded from this obligation.

Key Terms
محرم (mahram): A person related by blood (nasab) with whom marriage is permanently prohibited, such as siblings, parents, children, uncles, aunts, etc.
أهلية الإرث (ahliyyat al-irth): Capacity to inherit; being among those who could potentially inherit from the person, irrespective of actual inheritance at the time.
زمن (zamin): A person suffering from zamanah, meaning loss of limbs (hands and/or feet) leading to incapacity.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the Hanafi ruling in the passage, upon whom is maintenance of a mahram relative obligatory?
A) On any relative, regardless of wealth
B) On a wealthy person for a mahram relative who is needy (minor, poor female, disabled, blind) according to inheritance share
C) On the actual inheritor after death
D) On the father regardless of need

Key Takeaway
Maintenance of mahram relatives is wajib based on need and potential inheritance, not actual inheritance.
